O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear sons, I have completed this book which is the culmination of medical science gathered together with its applications, and I have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in my vision, I came to understand that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is flourishing in our region and has spread far and wide, so much that this knowledge and art have been lost and dissected, and nothing remains from it except for small descriptions in old books that the hands have used.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and vanity have arisen, closing off thoughts and distancing knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I should revitalize this treatise in a single order following the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will come together with the forms of the cautery tools, and other instruments for work along with their adjustment of declaration and preparation as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled masters are found in our times, the art of medicine has been lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who intervenes in this to ascend into the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the location of the members, and their forms, unions and separations of the organs, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles, and the number of bones, and their movement patterns and rest positions, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus says Hippocrates that with speech it is much, and with deed it is little; and in the art of hands especially.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that anyone who is unaware of the matters previously mentioned risks making mistakes and wasting people's time; just as I have seen many times, numerous individuals who interfere in this field and abandon their studies and lack of practical experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	And I saw a fool who treated a woman's neck abscess and cut the arteries in her neck; because so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in an elderly man, and the stone was large; he took with it a part of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And indeed, I have already called upon the art of draining pus, and observed the position of the illness and the size of the stone, and if one were to treat it properly they would likely die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I have seen another place where the cure was given to one of our country's Duke who had broken his leg, and along with the break there was an injury; and these places were full of ignorance causing the breakage upon the injury in various ways through strong anger, and did not leave any rest on the injury throughout; and thus ended after .i. term (3 months); and they commanded that he not break it again; and waited until the leg was fully swollen and the feet and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I have been summoned to come to him, and I hurried to come to relieve the leg; and when I heard it dislocated so much that he was in peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But any path of corruption had already been confirmed within the body or member, and could not be cured; and the process of corruption continued through the member until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see one other site that collapses an incision into an abscess, and then inflames due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is full of melancholic humor, does not require iron to be touched if it cannot be removed in part so that all the corrupted parts can be taken out.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear children, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: meaning, where there are dangers in multiple situations; and I will show in each part of this book where there is danger and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Because this is necessary that you guard yourselves, so that the common folk cannot wrongly speak of you. Take your weapons into consideration, and treat your ailments lightly yet firmly, and use the best way so through the grace of God you come to salvation and be healed; and leave fearful diseases to the relief of health; and remove from those who cause you doubt the instruments used on you, have faith in yourself that you can come from this world to glory in the other.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiens states in some of his admonishments: "Do not treat any illness wrongly, lest you be called foolish by the common folk.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medicine cauteries, and the chapters are arranged from the head down to the stones; and on the forms of instruments, and iron tools for cauteries, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are arranged with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and they are arranged from the head down to the stones, and include the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we remind ourselves of the work, it is necessary for me to discuss the quality and harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and the harm, are the longest speech and most subtle science and the secrets answered. And these were spoken about by many wise people, and they agreed with this; and their words satisfy me somewhat, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery universally aids all compositions or where there is matter, for it applies to two compositions: these being known as warm composition with matter, and dry composition with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the warm and dry combined with matter, there was no agreement and they said that the fire cautery is a great help; and the other ones said the opposite: that the fire cautery only helps diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be treated with heat or drying for a disease that comes from heat and dryness. And someone who says the opposite, claiming that the cautery provides great help to hot and dry diseases that come into people's bodies,
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and its moisture to the character of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every method, do not interfere with it unless the one who has proven it does, and who knows through long use the art of cauterization, and the diversity of human complexion. And they understand the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the outbreaks and duration; we have no fear for other complexions, especially in cases of cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all things agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, children, that a fire-cautery contains secrets of treatments, and it brings more benefit than the burning medical cauterizing tool.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come out except from the member that is burned, and it harms no other member if I name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot medicines travel from limb to limb by repelling each other, and they bring about diseases of healing through this process; and sometimes the illness strikes the patient. Fire, due to its high quality and goodness in substance does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, and it corresponds to the truth of things; and for this, I apologize for the length of speech, because I do not want to withhold from you the secret of fire, and its quality, how it relieves diseases of the body, as the philosopher says by demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they determined when the cauterizations should be done, and studied the prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable at all times, because the harms arising are diminished by the aid of the fire cautery; and moreover if the cauterizations are for necessary pains that cannot wait until greater evil befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like the foolish, child; for a disease cured by cauterization has no return; and they say it this way. But it is not as they believe, because cauterizations are only medicine that alters the complexion, dries out the fluids causing pain, and is valued more than medicine for its swiftness in enhancing strength, and due to the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that diseases come at no time according to the complexion of the disease and its place, gathering in him excesses through the acquisition of meats and similar things. If not cauterizations administered within him where there is little excess and moisture, like cauterizations for pain and such things, then this kind of pain does not return; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And there are few people who understand why cauterizations are called the ends of medicine, and this is seen; but they do not believe that cauterizations follow after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is said that cauterizations follow in medicine because when we administer methods of treatments for any illness and if they don't work, then we administer our cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus clearly understood, cauterizations are indeed the ends of medicine, not according to the understanding of others.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauterizations made from metal tools are better than those made of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and its high nature; and they said that gold cautery blades do not cause decay, but this is not true as I have proven it and found out that it is true in some people; and gold cauterizations are worth more than iron ones, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And still, when you heat the gold tool, you do not realize that it is heated by the color of the gold, and then it cools off quickly; and if it is heated too much; should be put in the fire; thus there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use our iron cautery that we have equipped for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have ordered this chapter on the old shoulder until the elbow, because it makes finding it easier.
dou cautere olivaire	wooden cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The fire cautery works against moisture and cold on the head, and there are two ways to perform this due to illness called "soda," and because of many bodily fluids that drain from the head as hair, and ears, and due to a multitude of dreams, tooth pain, throat pain, and most especially for all diseases resulting from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient's body is cleansed by dissolving medicine, modifying the head. Three times or four times, according to how well the properties and heat and habit of the ailment can be endured; and then again after the head of the ailment.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place it between your hands, and press your hands onto the sides of your nose; afterwards, place the root of your palm on the root of their nose between their two nostrils; and when your middle fingers arrive, if there is bleeding from this point, warm the cautery which is called 'olivare', and its form is as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place his head in its usual position with ink, and draw slowly and steadily as you adjust your hand a little at a time; then lift your hand alone, and check if the bone comes into view when you see it is only .i. sol (a small unit of measurement) underneath; if you do not see the bone, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after that, take .i. poc (another unit of measurement) of flour, and place it in a moistened soft cotton inside, then put on his head, and let him keep it for .iij. jors (days); afterwards, put some buttered meal on the wound; and leave until the scalding is gone; after that treat the wound with ointment known as 'tetrafarmaçon', until it has healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they were told by the old ones that when a wound remains open longer, more pus comes out; and for this reason it moves.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they were told that we should continue applying the cautery until part of the bone is burned; and then when what is burned from the bone has been done, it should be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other says that we must apply the cautery here and press so hard that we lift as much of the bone as one small twig would be by women putting it into their tubes for when body fluids flow out. And should we leave the wound open for a long time; after that, we must clean and heal it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good in all respects, except when there is a path of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the shoulders are weakened by the continuous drainage from nature, as we demonstrate on other limbs; and even if the shoulder of disease is weak through nature, and my first sign of cautery heals better for me, and I use this method in essence gather together salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head comes chronic pain and lasts long, one must use the patient's herbs and pills which are called 'cochies', and treatments for cleansing of the head and ears and bandages; and if one applies the cautery as we have mentioned before, it is useful.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the shoulder of the sick is of strong nature, and it should not be too cold; therefore apply the cautery under this one for a bit as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After apply the cautery to each horn of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and do one more application in the neck area which is called 'wheels'; and do another application under where suction cups are put; and move your hand so that you don't go past the bone: the patient feels too much pain in this cautery compared to others, I will speak about it elsewhere; and it's necessary that the horn applications are more subtle than when applying to the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly pain comes in one part of the head,
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine cautery involves taking a spoonful of vinegar, and using the peel and its residue on both sides for about two inches around each head; then apply this vinegar mixture exactly where the pain resides in such a way that you can spread it under the skin; and when it has spread well, press it tightly like that for 12 hours; afterwards remove the vinegar bandage and let the wound heal naturally for another two or three days; then put on a clean bandage with butter until a scab forms.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is purified; and if you notice that you are applying any of the burning medicines I have written about or the first volume on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery proceeds according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery as it is described here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a bell or has .i. point of curvature, and in the middle there's a small appearance; put it over the painful area, and hold your hand and gently move the iron, until half of the thickness of the flesh at the knee is burned; then lift your hand to prevent the artery from burning, which has been exposed, and allow an abundance of blood to flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing this in the area to be sewn, leave it on the affected area for three days; then change to cotton soaked with butter and apply it. Continue treating the wound with ointment until purified; if you wish to cauterize this migraine using the cautery known as "cultellare" at its tip, take care not to cover the artery in this migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	Regarding the treatment of headaches,
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraines as we have previously discussed in the divisions of diseases, and if it doesn't help, and you find that the heat treatments mentioned before concerning medicine and steel don't work, then you must heat the cautery called 'cultellare' until it turns white; and do this so that your tool is touching one line from half a degree long on the skin, and use your hand once, pulling it so that you don't cut an artery and stop just before reaching bone; and guard against the jaw becoming silent when eating, and make sure only the tongue is to be silent and spasm does not affect the patient, and guard against bleeding from the artery if it's been cut, or cutting with great fear and even those who are unaware of these procedures and have no experience in them; and leave the work halfway done; but I will tell you how to stem blood when an artery is cut, and show you where this is mentioned in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that the previous cauteries don't seem to help for this illness, and the patients are suffering, use them on the opposite side of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see that they tolerate it, administer the cautery mentioned in us or chapter on extracting an artery, with a two-bladed cautery; and these cauteries are better than the others and more useful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from cold in the ear, and we have applied solutions of medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and if the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery which is called 'pains', as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the cautery to all parts of the affected ear, or around the two points where the pain is located in both ears, and then move away slightly from the root of the ear after you have marked its location; apply ten points around each ear; after that treat the area until it heals properly.
de la torture de la bouche	of the pain in the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Pain that should be cured by a cautery does not encompass those caused by pus, as we have stated in sections on diseases; and no cautery should be applied to symptoms originating from dryness and rashes of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this symptom of pain caused by pus from ears and nasal discharge as well as phlegm in the head and gargle, and if it doesn't respond to treatment, then it's necessary that you apply three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, and another a bit beyond the temple area, and the third for aligning the two lips; place the cautery on the healthy part of the body, and have the patient receive the application right where pus may be found above the ear, slightly under the head's horn, and in the temple area to a length as long as one inch; keep the cautery over this until half the inside of the ear is burned; this is the form of the application.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the symptom of cuteria which we described earlier, but it's slightly more subtle; so when you treat the hand as I explained before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with an old case of apoplexy and you treat it as we have said, if it does not benefit and the patient has a fever, then you should apply three cautery treatments: two on the two horns of the head, and one on top of the head, and one where the neck is called 'vassel' as we have mentioned before. And the fourth application of the cautery is to be done near the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said previously.
de litargie	from alchemy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, you should give the patient large pills that purify the brain; after that, take back the head of the sick person all around, and place the camphor plaster on the occipital area; and here is the way to do cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it goes well like this, then it's good; and if not, do three applications of the fire cautery descending from head to collarbone, leaving an interval of one finger-width between each application. And treat it as with the others, and if you see that it has adjusted, and the patient is suffering, do another application in the middle. If necessary, two more on the two horns, and keep treating until it heals; and let the applications called "olive" be those previously mentioned.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cooling of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to cleanse the head of warts and what we have discussed previously. After treating the head with the patient, then apply fire cautery around the wart and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine below the collarbone; and if you need more applications, and the limb is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is extensive, then do four more cauterizations on the spine of the back. And leave it until the most sensitive part becomes dry, and raise your hand; afterwards treat it until it heals, and let those applications be called "olive" as we said previously.
de l’epilempsie	Of the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use the cautery for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first modify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section where the patient experiences large ailments and suffers from lack of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the child cannot endure it, make them gargle and chew, modifying the brain often with good meats; after that, insert the head halfway in water, and then apply one cautery as we have said previously, and another on the vessel, and each horn; and if the patient experiences pain, apply cauterizations like I have explained for those with paralysis and softness of limbs, on the spinal column and neck area, and use olive wood cauterization according to the method that I mentioned.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	And if the ailment is in a child, perform one fine cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the excesses or fluids are corrupted and thickened, therefore apply the fire cautery of the parts like we have said earlier to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to the cause of melancholy, these excesses decline into melancholy and leave the body with wet malaise, then let him drink something so that his brain may be cleansed, as was stated in the previous section on this subject.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After removing the head of the malaise; after make .i. linen thread well done, as .i. circle, if you put it around the head; and let the malaise sit in place, and is held well from all sides; after apply the liniment, and use butter from an old goat; and warm the head gently so that the patient can bear it; then empty the circle from within with the aid of the head, and let it cool; and do this to each malaise once a week with different governance properly, until they are cleared.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see that burning, do it making several points across the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautering increases the moisture in the brain; and then place wet cotton on butter and lard grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the power of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the power of the eyes first arises through the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and continue to instruct the patient to consume something purifying for the head, and protect it from all moisture. Make him sweat or take baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After having him drink after his head, and I have him cauterized near the head, and I perform two cauterizations on each of the two temples once the weakening due to eye power has reached both eyes together, or when only one temple is affected; and apply all the cauterization over all the veins and arteries that are within the skull, and ensure the cauterization lasts as long as the width of the temple; and guard against bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with a piece of material in such a way as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and cutting the cautery site, how to properly conduct it; every time one performs a cautery or ligature operation, do not perform it over the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the path of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes have been longstanding and accustomed, and are located on the veins, or over the arteries that are beneath the surface towards the head's appearance; one sees that they are cold excesses of phlegm, thus I apply the cautery that I mentioned at the beginning of this work concerning the descent to the eyes: .i. a cautery near the eye socket, and .ij. cauterizations on both temples, and .ij. cauterizations where ligature is done over the two bones; and if it requires more, then carefully cauterize above the eyelid with every .i. small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	through the eyes from within tears
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it doesn't benefit, then give three roes of wine to the patient. Afterward, heave the head up, and apply a cautery or olive oil in its middle; and make two applications of the cautery which is called "clavilis" on the two ears, just below the hair. And beware not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is weakened by illness and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which it is described here:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it's been done twice with the fire cautery on each of the two nipples as long as they are there; and don't let your hand go until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the method I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	The hair that touches the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	None of the times has it happened that the hair of eyebrows turns into the gums and touches the eye; in this case, you do a cautery according to two methods: namely with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are long and even, then command the patient to let them grow in health; after that, on the piece of paper for the eyes, draw a figure so as to resemble a leaf of myrtle, and make its beginning like the sign between the hairs; then place wet cotton soaked in egg glue and garlic paste onto the eye, then heat up the cautery tool which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing over the figure you have drawn little by little several times, until the scabs are dry in that place; and the signs of healing from the operation are that you see the paper shrinking, and the hairs lifted to the edge of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then place wet cotton in butter as long as the scorching is removed; after ointment treatment until it becomes clean.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if hairs and the paper become softened after this, then resume the cautery on that same spot as you did initially; and when the hairs have fallen out, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural position, is even, and doesn't stick to the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fire cautery of medicine commands that the patient allow hairs to grow until they are large and even; then make the form of parchment like the leaf of myrtle. Then take French soap and live coal from a flame, each one of them is an ounce, and grind them together well; and make haste so it does not cool down, then spread it on the form you made as like the leaf of myrtle, put it on the paper under the eye. If the disease lasts for one day only, you must open it in one place, and if in both places similarly; and fill each hole with wet cotton similar to an egg; let the patient's head be in your healthy hands and place your finger showing over the medicine, press once every time the patient feels the irritation of the medicine, as they also feel irritation like from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the mordification has passed, if you lift the heel from awe, and reward it if you see that paper lifted as if it had been lifted by the constraint of fire or through an incision; and if it is like this, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is not healed this way, then one still has to apply medicine on the limb or wait for the medicine to take effect until your symptoms are equal and your eyesight's point is met; afterwards place moistened cotton in butter until the burn from the ointment leaves, after cure the wound from the grease that is called 'dyafenis' and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to take care of your work well by careful attention so that no medicine leaks into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper gets wet after that, and the hair touches in the eye, then renew the medicine on the soft part of that limb which is made moist by the clean paper; do this as you did before; cure it until it heals; and this is the form of the leaf of mirtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and do not have the right way respond to him who studies this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you are treating a fistula as we have said in the sections on diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you apply the cautery using this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy position; and cut the hair on their head between your hands in such a manner that it doesn't move or shift; afterwards, put moist cotton, akin to an egg's lining or garlic juice, on their eye; next, heat up the cautery which is divided: and while above the head, shape it as you would with a goose feather, assembling it so that the cautery sits there; if you see it, let it be pointed from one end of the head to the other, and if you see it, allow it to resemble a tent; but in any case, whatever is above serves well for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp. de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.
