Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be sure to handle it carefully so you don't break it, and leave a part of it, causing greater pain from the wisdom of the root than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be aware that you should not do it like ignorant surgeons, who break the tooth once due to their haste and boldness, and don't correct themselves as we have advised. But instead, they bring about this frequent operation due to this great disease from the roots where they stay or because of the tooth they break, just as we often wish. And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the mouth with wine or vinegar; and if bleeding occurs after, which happens quite frequently, wash your mouth with vitriol juice; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, to which you first get your teeth into, should be long pointed and have big handles, so they do not bend when you pull on the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large members that do not bend while pulling, and be made of well-made iron, and be toothed for gripping.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to place wet cotton with butter inside for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the bones are pulverized, and indeed, place the forceps known as "algfi" where it seems that the physician's bone should be; they must also be made inside like a file, which is its form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these tongs, then you must uncover the entire flesh right up to the root, and place the tool known as "altalhi", which is essentially a spike, in that manner:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it so that neither breaks or swells, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good; if not, use all the tools you have, as their forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if help is taken from this tool which has two prongs, as its form is shown here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the order of teeth, and this tool which seems like a large pair of tongs, as its form is shown:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this tool be such that it cannot break, and know that few tools of bone exist; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the skilled surgeons find their instrument by themselves, according to what their work and disease show them, for there are parts of diseases where old instruction did not teach a tool because of the diversity among others and if it breaks from wear or from the rest of bones, or if it decays, so he searches among the tools that suit him, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, as is described here:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And may they be large and well holding to hold the bone, so that it doesn't escape but can be held and removed; and then restore at its place with medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and if it is small, then use all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in virgins, it's necessary for you to know whether the tooth was born after another one, and wasn't placed straight, and can't be pulled or filed: then pull it out; and if it is together with a tooth, take this instrument described here, which resembles two small hooks, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is extracted bit by bit in my hands due to its hardness, and because you do not move others, and if it can be seen that one could grind it out, then I will grind down with one part of the file as this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used to make needles; and I grind the tooth bit by bit in my hands lightly, so that you do not move until it finishes; then make it flat at the end with all tools, and if it's too sharp and irritates the tongue, then you should grind down the roughness until it is even, so as not to irritate the tongue or damage speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth swells
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front of the gum line, through percussion or mashing, and when the patient can't press into it what they chew without defecating, and once you've treated them with restricting medicines, if this fails; then they must be restrained by a golden thread because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never does; choose threads that are neither too thick nor too thin depending on the space between the teeth. And when you see to straighten teeth, take the thread and the double needle between two healthy teeth, then place the dislocated tooth in between diseased teeth if there is one or more, until you can perceive a healthy tooth from another side; then start covering again up to where you previously covered, and gently and skillfully tighten your hand, until it doesn't move. And secure your tie at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then hold the teeth with a thread on some pincers, and join them together, putting them back between the healthy tooth, and then place it so as not to irritate the tongue; and leave it like this as tight as he can endure, if it slips or the threads come undone, tie it again with another thread; if it stays here and serves thus throughout its duration, and this is the form of the teeth and the layout of the two healthy teeth, and of the two middle ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is lost, you set it back to its place piece by piece as we have explained; and do not interfere with anything that is not fit and endure pain, nor at any time make the shape of a bone tooth from a cow, and put it in the place where the defect exists, and tighten it as we have said, and stays like this serving for as long as possible.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of the cords that come from under the tongue or its natural position when we are born; or by accident during a healed wound; and the operations should be such as you work on the mouth with the patient, place your head in good health, lift the tongue; then tie the nervous cord as wide as necessary until the tongue is displaced from its position. If there's stiffness or swelling, especially if it's due to an immediate healing of a wound, clip off the hook and tie again more widely. And be sure that the cut isn't too deep because there might be an artery under it; when you're done, then lift the head until it turns pinkish-red or blue, then put on ice underneath the tongue; and treat each night so that they don't stick together.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes out, then put sulfur on the wound; and if it does not heal, then apply slow-burning cautery which is good for this; afterwards treat with other remedies until the healing is done.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it's of any color or black or hard, and the patient doesn't feel it, don't touch it because it's a boil; and if it's turning towards pus, and there's moisture, then use the hook tool to puncture it with a subtle incision from both sides, and heal it from one side and the other; and if it doesn't stop draining in your procedure, place vinegar on it until it is healed completely. Then return to your procedures as long as you are using force; then lift the head from coolness and perspiration, and apply further healing methods until it's fully recovered.
des apostemes de la gorge	extracting abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No time comes within the throat canals that are called "godath", and they're properly known as the two almond-shaped glands. When you treat them, like we said in the division section, and if they aren't healed yet, then be careful: if these are firm, small, sensitive lumps with a reddish color, don't touch them even with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they're red and the root is large, don't touch them even with iron for blood flow. Leave them until they heal, then you can remove them; or they might burst on their own. If they have a white coloration and the root is fine, prepare your tools to cover them, but first check if the abscess has resolved and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand in front of the sun, and have their head under your control, and the operation makes them open their mouth and the surgeon presses the tongue down to all the instrument, as this is how it's done; and have the tools made from silver or thin steel just like knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the pus-filled blister? Take one and put it into the almond, then pull it upwards more than you can; remove nothing from the threads, then extract with the tool, as depicted here; it looks like a force. And both the head is placed upright, and one part after another are extremely sharp, and made of iron or silver.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool at hand, use tweezers instead, as depicted here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make cuts on one side and the other name; and when you have performed one of the almonds, perform the other in the same manner, and after cutting gargle the patient with hot and cold water, as well as a gentle flow of blood occurs, then gargle with hot water or slices from cooked cherry tomatoes or laurel leaves, and similar things, until the saliva is fully cleansed; then continue the cure until it is healed; and no other abscesses are born in the throat than the two almonds, so perform them accordingly like the two almonds evenly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is called the small abscess; and had tightly closed all of the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage and could neither eat nor drink, and died if she remained like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses had risen so high that it had caused two rows of tears to form under each nostril.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly performed this operation and removed a lump from one side, then the other, extracting much pus. Then I made cuts on both sides of his neck near the jaw and opened up to see inside. After that I cleaned out these abscesses and took some part of them; only a little blood came out. And so after I performed all these steps, it was done, I let my patient swallow water and then wine, not stopping in cutting away from those abscesses for a long time; the abscesses began to grow back immediately filling up the space I had emptied, until it got quite large; then I closed them again by cauterizing inside the throat: thus he stopped growing. And I moved on from these parts and God did with him what happened after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When swelling descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is off in size being round, it is called 'eye'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it has been treated as we have said in the division, and the cure doesn't help, and you see that the extraction of pus is calmed, and it is subtle, then it's necessary to remove it; and that one which is round and assembled isn't long; and it's bloody or of a reddish color or black, so it's necessary for you to avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the patient.

Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said about its blench and length, you should have the patient face the sun, and press their tongue against the tool as we have described before; then insert the needle into the eye, pull it outwards, and remove it with the two tools mentioned in the incision of two almond-like objects.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it must be that you do not remove more fluid than is beyond the natural limit; for if you remove too much, it harms both speech and action. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears losing their sense of smell due to bleeding, it is necessary that you apply means for the cautery of their sense of smell.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is by hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And when the patient's sense of smell returns to your health, then press their tongue with the tool we have mentioned or as explained in the treatise on cautery, and pour in fresh, sharp water, ensuring it is neither too thick nor too thin; and use the movement of that tool, which is described here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have a hair where I apply the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and place the tool over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient rest with their head on its side so that saliva and the mucus flow from their mouth to the medicine inside, but not down to the throat or causing pain; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see that it has dried and the effects of the medicine are reduced; and if you see this, take cotton and envelop it with any tool, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the tool on top of the cotton on wax, so that the cotton burns into the eye while it's damp; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for four to five days. And if you need to repeat the medicine cautery procedure, then do it again, after which clean around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean off anything left of the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargling until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or using the cautery; if it's treated with fumigation in this way, take calendula and ipecacuanha and oregano and rue and chamomile and lettuce and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them into one pot, put them there, and bring it to a boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot place two sticks according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it's silver or iron, and if one of the shoulder bones is placed in the mouth against the patient as long as the vapor rises to the testicle through the scrotum until the testicle is necrosed; after this be repeated often, until the testicle dries out. And ensure you do not perform this at the beginning of the abscess eruption, because many things occur; and do not carry out this procedure when the abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a reed and put an eggshell in the patient's mouth, so that the heat of the wound does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not allow steam to accumulate on the mouth, and together with these remedies it provides good treatment for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, you may use the os or spine of a fish bone, with no need for anything else; if so, then it is suitable that you remove what you can see, and press your tongue against the sun on all the tool, until you see movement. de la sansue de la gorge	from the saliva of the throat

li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Holes for discharges resemble what memory recalls from one to another in this book, and they differ in puncturing and sizing; and there are two ways to do this, with one being similar to its appearance, and concerning moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for when the limbs are inside the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those in the foundation, and the abscesses in the inner flesh are different from those that come into joints, and each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And with abscesses one should not pierce them until the body is dead according to its development; and for those that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses beneath joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beneath joints, and if they are pus-filled inside, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint might be corrupted, which is a cause for contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is within the main limb, and if you delay puncturing until it's dead, it will harm the main limb. Or if it's within the foundation, then if you pierce through or in such a way that it becomes dead; it should not be that you puncture an abscess without proper digestion being completed, except for when it's within the foundation, which could inflame internally and lie deep inside, leading to fistulas; and cannot heal properly over a long period.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be known when the time for perforating an abscess that is dead according to its maturation, which is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and reduction of pain and flush, and the movement and firmness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be ensured that you place the perforation site above the abscess or as closely as possible to where it opens outwards, and if the perforation is along the length of the body, and if the abscess is located at hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	When they bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are within the fatty tissue, if there's any movement you must let the puncturing until proper digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce before that moment, then the poison from within spreads throughout his body and fills with heaps of filth; and by chance hardens his flesh and the underlying parts.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are no abscesses pierced through the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you apply small punctures, small cuts; and in large abscesses, large cuts, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses or if it requires a knife cut, and covering; when they have become as a piece of cloth, and are flattened, then you should do this as one does with infants: and those that split into three angles, and those that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of corners; and those where you make an oval-shaped cut, and other cuts and cutting shapes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary to fully pierce them. And when the abscess is large and has formed a large lump, you should pierce it, but not drain all of the pus at that moment, rather only remove a portion; then stop the pus until the other side, then leave nothing hanging down immediately after; do this repeatedly from large to small, until the pus comes out entirely. Likewise if the body has weak strength, or pregnant women, or young children, or elderly and decrepit individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when one tries several times with blood coming out, perhaps killing the patient, you should not neglect this.

Therefore be cautious of this chapter, and when you have made your incision, if there is a wound, look at the size of the wound from the incision; and if it's clear-cut, use linens or pieces of cotton to apply; and if it's large with many pus pockets, then it is necessary that for each you make a tent so they stick together; and if you have cut into some part of the skin in your incision and sewed it inside, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind up to three days; then set it and treat with ointment until it heals.

And if bleeding continues, apply government and treatment, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it's or near a stream, and the area where the operation took place or the abscess is mostly nervous, then you should put on mosquito nets and cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it's on skin, and the wound is fleshy, then you should apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil until the third day as we have said; and then remove the dressing and wipe and treat as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to understand universally in the treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here begins this chapter.

des scrophules	of the scrofula

And each scrophula is properly within its coat, as the nut and the abscess at the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrophulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to submit to treatment.

And if you cut the vein or artery, and it doesn't allow opening, then put vitriol paste in the wound, or any powders that stop blood flow, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscess subsides, and the wound softens, and begins to rot.

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	And it is necessary that you understand how to treat its root, drain the pus, and stitch as we have said.

Those scrophula that have excess, puncture where it opens; and puncture in this manner as previously mentioned, while depending on it. de squinance	regarding obliquity
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of how to make an incision in the throat; but I never saw anyone do it here, and this is written down from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinting vision, it is necessary that the incision made in the throat which is called 'epiglottis' be avoided; and one should not offer aid by this method, because all the veins and the heart are close to the patient who has pus in their mouth or in the throat or between two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the channel of the heart, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we cut through three or four small slits across, between the two circles or by the size of the slit thereon, not within the cartilage; and such a cut makes it suitable for cutting the epiglottis so that no flesh remains, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary for them to stretch the throat skin all the way up to the trachea, then cut through the windpipe until it reaches the chest; and avoid the blood vessels, should you see any thing at all, and then close that wound site as we have said; and this has been demonstrated by the section of the blood stream of the windpipe which jumps out from the ruptured area, and by lack of voice function; and leave the incision open for a bit.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed where one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound as neatly as possible, and all the skin without the cartilage; then administer medicines that create flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis insists that one should not perform this until the throat is entirely blocked, and the patient is judged dead, and the defect is evident.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then stitch up the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally, and they will breathe through the wound, hence keeping them alive from death; this was according to the instruction that the elders would leave the wound open until the disease's malady has passed, which indeed passed after three or four days. And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and clean it, until it had healed; and I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I witnessed a maiden who took the knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe. And I was summoned to heal her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found that blood was issuing from it, and indeed, there wasn't a cut or exit for the blood other than the throat, and the wind flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed and cleansed the wound as well as I could until she was healed; and to the maiden there was nothing left but for her to be hoarse, and she returned after that to her usual state. For this reason I say that in the crafting of the epiglottis, one should not fear.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts called "gullet hernia" are known as large cysts with a blackish hue, and they occur frequently in women. They can happen in two ways: naturally or by accident; natural ones do not have an opening.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidents occur in two ways, of which one resembles fat we know, and the other way resembles cysts coming from us through an artery; there is fear here, and it does not involve making incisions except for small ones. Only do this if you are able to thoroughly examine every part: If you find it just like fatty tissue that cannot reach any vein, cut it out as you would cut fat, and remove it together with its outer cover, if there's anything left; thoroughly search everywhere and cure it appropriately until it is completely healed.
des nous	from now on
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are there to treat us, of which I will mention all the similarities; now it is fitting that I explain the entire distinction between us and what follows.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the body's secretions have passed and putrefaction has occurred; then, the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new, there is no fever or pain and contains pus, which is its own sac and is in accordance with the color of the body's flesh and begins similarly to a boil, becoming large; and are according to two appearances, greasy or moist, and much of the color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treating the new, that you first test and inquire about all the instrument which is called 'intromissor', according to what its shape comes or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of probing pus in us is that you seek the greasiest part of it than what you find in the abscess and twist your fingers a little by a little until you know that the instruments have reached the body, then as according to the size of the abscess; then extract the pus, and take care not to break.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture cuts through it, whatever color it has, if you do as I said of the other abscesses; and if after the incision no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then cut accordingly like what I have said about the others, and once it doesn't come out with forceps again, take hold of it with tweezers and lightly scrape off each side and remove the bandage where it was located, for you must pull the whole thing clean along with the nodule; and if you cannot pull it clean, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if nothing remains and it reoccurs many times; and if some does remain but doesn't bother you, use powders that are corrosive to fill the wound, hold the wound still, place hot wadding on the abscesses, and treat it with other treatments until it is clean. And if there is a lot of pus, sew up two sides of the wound, and treat what is covered by the bandage.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too close to be treated in opposition or otherwise if there's urgency, then use the site of vitriol juice and let it take its course for two or three days, as long as the wound heals, and rest with the boiling of blood; then return to coppering where some has remained from new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the surgical instruments used for incision, they come in three ways: large, medium, and small. There are also three that are called 'albaret', and one that is referred to as 'breb'. They exist in three types: large, medium, and small, for enclosing abscesses and fistulas. They are like needles used for tying threads, made of arnica citrin, iron or silver. The yellow ones work well with blacking for encircling the bends of fistulas. There are three kinds according to the quantity of the width of the perforations: large, medium, and small.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of knives resemble these: large, medium, and small. There are also incision blades with two bends in three ways; those with three bends and are also in three ways; there are blades with two bends and single-bend blades as well, all in three varieties. All these are necessary according to their type.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this person they sharpen, and among these there are who do not cut with force but only from one side; thus we burn their noses, because in this case one neither cuts the vein nor the nerve. And of these intrusive instruments, the blades are placed in handpieces, so that the patient does not notice at the opening of abscesses; and they come in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and none is used to exert force except in soft flesh, like legs, arms, nipples, and elbows, and alike among them; and in no other case do we use another tiny instrument resembling excisions on the penis, according to this form, to which one stops blood flow:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once in the healthy part that closely divides veins and arteries, and not according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	None of the men's nipples swell when they begin to become corrupted, until they resemble women's nipples; and they remain swollen and puffed up, and those who want to cure them should do so according to this form of this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Trim the fat then apply medicine to the wound's edge. Then stitch together both edges of the wound and treat it until it heals fully. And if the chest is tilted downward due to size like in women, cut through this into two stich lines above by similar splits; making one connect with the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape here: from here .b.to here .g. Then burn off the skin between the two edges and remove the fat. Apply what we have described about stitching and powders as well as necessary treatments until it heals fully. And if it has not healed or the incision is not complete, because the body will not settle or due to blood leaking out during treatment, it's necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; leave this until the ointment and fat can be removed then treat it further until fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	removal of abscesses and gallstones
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Wounds that occur from abscesses are manners of hard scrophulas, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should have their cuts made according to this form, from line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment as needed until the wound heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble smallpox, then cut them as we have said in cuts of smallpox, and if the wound is clean, then apply the cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When it comes to an artery, and the skin is stitched where it's open, many times pus forms, and just like with that at a punctured vein and pus; and if one knows this when it's due to an artery, then the pus will be long and full; and when you feel it with your fingers, you'll sense constriction; and when it's about a vein, there is no leakage or appearance of pus; and treating such pus is foolishness, and similarly when it is amidst wounds and swellings, and elsewhere like in the neck and around mutton or other parts, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid the iron cure, and that for the head should also be avoided. When it comes to one who is inflamed by an artery, they should sew above the skin as long as possible; then perform tailoring at the inch marks, and beautifully separate the artery from the tissues, until it's fully revealed; then insert a probe under this one, and pierce till the other side, and tighten the artery with double thread on both sides according to what I have taught you in extracting the two arteries that are in temples; then cut off the area between the two lines using an intervening thread as long as there is pus flowing through it, and thereby release the pus; then apply the cure that dries out thereafter until the string lets out pus; then treat this with ointment until it heals; and if the pus comes from the vein's size, you should color your hand with the contents of the pus over all the skin. Then insert a needle under the skin you hold in your hand, pierce it, and have double thread ready so that you pull it on the other side; then tie the pus, as I have said, or tie threads from both parts to both shoulders using this string; and if you doubt whether the string lets out pus, you should insert another needle under all the pus near the first hole and tighten the strings in four places; then cut off the excess pus until it stops flowing, then cut away the excess with scissors and leave what is tied. Then place a moist cloth covered in wine and oil on top of one side, then apply cures and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	abcesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As with pus that comes into the artery and vein, pus enters the lungs when they are cut, or due to excessive labor, and similar occurrences.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often with shoulders and elbows and in all places where joints are present. And this is the case for pus filled abscesses, and their color seems to be like that of flesh, and exists in many positions without pain; and when they are restricted in form, if feels as if the body is hurting, but not throughout, only around the bone; and moves well from all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and one who is in joints should not cover with iron: there might be a contraction by accident; and that which is at the head or forehead causes the skin to become inflamed.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, if you have tweezers, and pinch them at their base; and if they are large, if you suspend them up to the elbow, and slice, then scrape, then extract the pus, and then suture the wound together. And treat until it heals properly.
des grosses boces pendans	Large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	In every abdomen and nowhere else appears the lumpul, it is a disease which is called 'fungus' by its appearance, and has a subtle root, and large heads; there are small ones and very big; I saw one person who had two bellies that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, had tiny roots, were cracked, and corroded from moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I found them in the first one weighing XVIII onces (around 360 grams), and in the second one VI З. (around 120 grams). In the incisions, if you observe that the tissues are moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist with a subtle root; when you touch it, it feels like fat under your hand, and you should apply the fire cautery to it.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when the surgeon comes there are many times great blood losses, and if it cannot be avoided, then quickly use a cautery; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful from the incision of the iron, take a well-made thread and bind the tool as we have said, and leave for two days; and then restrain, and do not cease to pull on the thread until it catches the tool, with no trouble; and if the roots are large, fear catching them by the belly, but you can well catch half of them, then cauterize so that they don't swell up again; then treat the wound, and make sure you do not catch the wire which is of pale color and has little sense and milk appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene next.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bile flows freely
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	The appearance of the boil comes from the cauterization of wounds or tears in the scrotum, and it is on the abdomen and there are some boils, as happens in other ruptures, or blood that leaks from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned previously, or due to windiness; and if it's through the rupture in the scrotum and through the opening of the boil, its color resembles the color of the pus, and is a light thing without pain, and opens from diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the passage of an intestinal obstruction, then it is more varied, and when one presses it with their fingers if it returns, and then comes back, and by chance if it gets stuck, and expands quite a bit at the entrance during bathing and due to strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's due to moisture, it's a simple matter and opens well when you press with your hand, not restraining; and if it's due to blood, open through these signs the large and hard abscesses, and they penetrate according to an amount; and if it's due to wind, it stings at the finger, and the pus is such that you should look to see whether its appearance is due to arterial or venous blood, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you allow the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have explained in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
