And repeat the process until the bladder is emptied, and properly guide the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	About diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction has assembled there, and you see distilled waters and medicines, if make all the tool which is called 'clepsydra', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three parts: two from one side and one from the other, as you see; and cut through this with medicine in such a way that it numbs well the member without addition, if possible to drain the moisture and then set when necessary; and when you see your medicines flowing into the bladder, place the head of the instrument into the moisture, and direct them towards the person administering; if you extract the moisture from the instrument, apply pressure on the one who is applying it immediately afterwards; if you do this while extracting the moisture with the instrument, then set firmly after that; if moisture enters during this process, comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of a subtle stone with which we catheterize the bladder: thus far.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it's made of silver or an archaut, and the shoulder is placed higher. And from one side up to the first rib where it meets; then take a sheep's bladder and place in it the moisture that you're going to catheterize the bladder with, then connect it between the two ribs forming a thick double thread, and heat this part of the moisture on fire; then insert the head of the catheter into the member, then pull your hand towards the bladder until all the moisture comes out, so that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder. And if you can't reach the bladder, take a piece of parchment paper, and make a circle, punch it roundly in the middle; then tie this thread firmly at these points, heat this part of the moisture on fire; then assemble the circle as you would assemble a loop, and put inside what you see, the moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; do it like how you did with the bladder, press with your hand until all the moisture is in the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have discussed in detail the methods of stone dismemberment and extraction together with medicines; we also spoke about the differences between stones that are small like raindrops and all their signs, and when to open large stones; and I will explain this clearly and briefly for you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I state that stones which are small like raindrops in the bladder often occur in children, and this is a sign that an infection has jumped into the bladder similar to how it jumps through its delicacy; open the urethra, rub the painful areas of their penis, and let them urinate many times, then rest; and note these urinary jumps; and for a while after these jumps, the treatment of children is light until they are four years old, and becomes much more troublesome in the elderly, being in between childhood and age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by purging, in order to draw out all the toxins that are within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And it clogs up every time when trying to cut into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take hold of the patient by their limbs, and lift them up and move them backward, so that the stone drops down to beneath the bladder, and exits not from above; then have them sit between your hands, with their hands on their thighs, so that the bladder is fully sloping downwards; then try and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in space, now hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if they do not defecate all the way with touching, moisten your index finger of the left hand, for if the patient is young, or your middle finger, if the patient is older in age; and press into its foundation, touch the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, remove it from the neck of the bladder; then press up onto your finger, and push outwards where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to stretch up the testicles with his right hand, and with his left hand hold the skin over the testicles at the part where you will make the cut; then push out the spermatic cord, of which this is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between that which is between the coions and the foundation, not in the middle but at the edge of the left snowbank. And be straight on the stone, and your hands should touch or be close to the foundation, and make it of a round size going through so that it is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too big; by chance press if your hand is touching the foundation, then it will break easily without much effort. And know that there are parts of the stone where there are angles and edges: they get stuck in coming out; and at some parts which are under like a nut, resembling roundness, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And in the places where there are angles and edges, make the size bigger; if it doesn't break, then it's necessary that you use the pincers which are like a file at their tip to force the stone so that it does not escape; or you can push underneath with a delicate curved instrument at its tip; and if you cannot devise this way, then make it slightly wider than your little finger, and if it breaks cleanly, then force it with vinegar; and if there are more stones, then break out the biggest at the neck of the bladder first, then cut upwards, then apply pressure downwards, and the smaller ones later if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, one must tend her and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For these two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately where the blood cannot coagulate; but always strive for a pull, or a break with tongs, as long as you can extract it piece by piece. And when you have accomplished your task, fill the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, then tighten, and pour oil and wine over it, or oil and rose water and cold water to soothe the inflamed area; then bind the patient up on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release the tension, make sure to lift it with oil and water well, then apply a diapering ointment and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if the abscess bursts in the wound and chemical corrosion happens, or clots form inside the bladder, and thus urine retention causes it to be known like this without a leap with urine: therefore, you must tend the wound, extract that blood, because if it remains, it corrodes the bladder and deteriorates; then cleanse the wound with water and soap and salt, and assist him in all ways you see fit until he is well. And when you treat him, you should tie both legs of the patient, and gather medicines on his body.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it's located where the penis leads, being stuck there, and urine cannot come out; if you treat as I am saying, that you cut many times, and excuse the cuts made by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I already have this experience like this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron branch according to this shape, and have it fixed at three points on a stake:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the penis near the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently push the rod in the penis until it reaches the stone; and slowly twist the rod with your hand at the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from another side; if urine starts coming out, then press your hand on the part of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks suddenly and urine starts flowing out, wash the area with water, and be careful to avoid further injury. If you can't do this for any reason, tie the thread around the stone and another one above it, then position the penis between these two threads right at the site of the stone, pull forcefully, then remove the threads and clean off the coagulated blood in the wound; and continue treatment until there's no longer bleeding.
de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are found in women's bodies, and if they occur once, it requires special care, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to reveal herself through tears, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you understand the signs to know the outcome.

de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Gelatinous mucus is nothing else but a gathering of moisture or white pus, which exists within the coat of the kidneys, that contains the egg; and it's called 'pus', and there isn't any proper time when it's properly in the membrane of the egg if one considers there to be another egg. And this is the skin under the kidney containing the white pus we've mentioned; and it doesn't have its own space no.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the creation of this gelatinous mucus comes from weakness that affects the kidneys, and spreads that substance.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I state that the emorroids and the inflammation when they occur internally in the anus, and are not noticeable to touch, except for their treatment with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those at the mouth of the anus can be felt and those that can be treated are these.

Therefore, it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then place her on the altar of tongs, and hang the clothes on her roots, then cover with powder of medicines that restrict blood, such as senna and dragon's blood and incense, and similar substances; then soak her feet for an hour, then put them in cold water; and if bleeding persists, make her take a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gall and similar things, and then give her oat flour mixed with honey and garlic, and apply this plaster to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he stops bleeding, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu. des apostemes de la marris	The abscesses of the womb
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. de l’enfantement	Of childbirth

And when you see these signs, it's appropriate to gently press on her belly, so that the fetus exits quickly; because as it descends through her head, it also comes out with its remnants in proper parturition; and anything else that doesn't follow this process does not occur naturally.

des emorroydes	of lacerations

dou fremit	with tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part. de la forme dou clistere	of the bladder's structure
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never use an argentin or archaut bladder, or one made of melted silver or lead; and never use small or large utensils depending on who they are for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those utensils should be used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, as they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the bladder is either small or large, just like this:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if the belly is bound tightness or pain, as you see, and the head penetrates inside; let there be two holes on one side of it and one on the other; place medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment in this condition under the belly, letting the hole go all around through tiny slits, with each slit having about an inch of space between them. Then, insert one strong thread made of spun silk twisted into an 'X' or 'Q' shape inside each slit and stitch it together as if it were a goat; when the medicine is inside, tie it tightly with another strong thread in front of the instrument, then perform the enema; this forms a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and smear the head with oil or egg yolk or something similar on its face, then gently rub it. Then the doctor instructs his two helpers to hold his hands together, until all is visible, then remove the cyst, and lift the patient's legs at the surface, and if the medicine wants to come out, pull it as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, this gives more substantial aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you administer it during a colicky disease of the stomach, and the medicine rushes to escape, then repeat it as long as he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhage is from the root or base, or an abscess, then even a cyst as delicate as for a child; and this is the form of a delicate cyst where the skin is compressed:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in our division; now we will speak about treatments for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on how they are made, and where the wounds are made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The causes of injuries are through stone, the size of a sword or knife, or a lance or shaft or axe, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as an injury near the neck, or on the head, or chest, or belly, or liver, and other body parts. And I will tell you how to treat each wound, starting with simple injuries on the head, for memory will guide me in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound appears or bone is not broken, be careful if it's due to stone or similar things and the skin has been completely torn off, leaving large wounds. If you slightly doubt the presence of pus in those cases: if there's a little bleeding from the wound as soon as I clean the skull area itself, then treat that part normally instead; and encourage the patient to drink wine and eat fatty foods richly, as they help in healing.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they don't want to be treated surgically, reduce their meat intake and avoid drinking wine or eating large portions of meat. Instead, apply a moistened cotton in oil rose water, or in stictch wine only on the wound. If there is no pus present, apply it on fresh wounds where blood has just started flowing but hasn't been disturbed by air; then use the powder I will explain later. And if it's already been disturbed by air, apply some ointments until they heal completely.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar injuries, and the edges cannot be brought together by sutures, then join them with stitches, as I will say for abdominal wounds, regarding suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes bone, and blood, and only holds for a little while when supported; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace tough flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as roasted testicles and cooked wheat, as well as similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or discover that the skin has decayed, and it doesn't reach to the bone, then cut out all the decay, and let out pus, and then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without doubt, and it cannot be stopped with medicines, then tie the artery, and if you find that it's dislocated, then secure it with a thread; and if this doesn't prove beneficial, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put this powder which joins together like that when the heat of the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way to use the powder is like this: take one part of frankincense; dragon's blood two parts; living charcoal three parts, and finely ground it all into a powder, then apply it to the wound, and press it firmly until it well aerates and joins with its own blood thoroughly; and then bind it tightly, leaving it undisturbed if it doesn't swell; for you remove the medicine only when it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should only perform this bloodletting procedure once, not just because of the need for charcoal or dragon's blood, but when the surgeon has cleaned the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heart has healed the wound, even in that state, indeed do not apply this powder to it at all; but apply some digestible ointments or oat flour mixed with water and honey until it starts to heal. Then continue other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then use delicate forceps to extract them; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This injury comes from the neck, it is simple if there's no distinction between the neck and the head itself, but if the nerves in the neck or an artery has been severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, there is no other tool than to leave the treatment alone and not put anything restrictive on it, as this harms the nerves and causes them to withdraw; and don't apply anything cold to the wound because nerve substance is cold and continues with the brain which is in one of the highest members; but use gentle medicine like diluted rose water mixed with oil, and wash leaves also in mild water, and other earthy minerals done similarly, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, one should bend the edges and let it heal until it is clean.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, pierce them or start lower. If an artery is cut, and blood flows out, then expose it, repair it, and cauterize as needed; and if the spine of the throat, or ribs, or passage way is injured, guard it where the meat goes through, if you place the rib above the collarbone, without touching the throat but keep it according to its natural shape; and afterwards let him rest for some days, then cure it with dried herbs until it heals. And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, take those you can out, leave what you cannot reach until the wound discharges pus, dries up and clears the result; and if the wound is fresh, use a powder that I have said for that purpose.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a sinus, treat it as described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	From the wound caused by a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a spear or knife wound and the injury is deep, when you inspect the wound look for wind blowing out from it: if that happens, know the injury is fatal. And if it isn't deep and is still bleeding freely throughout its entirety, don't apply powder immediately or bind it straightaway because the blood wouldn't have time to clot properly causing leakage to heart and worsening of illness. Instead, apply an attractive ointment, binding twice a day. If you don't have an ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture and let the patient rest on the wound for 3 days or more; if no spasms occur, there will be no harmful heart tremors either. And when you notice good improvements, then know that the injury is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat then with other remedies as long as it is clean; and if it cannot be cleansed and healed, observe that there is a fistula; if the treatment proceeds as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is due to a sword or knife cut, and it's simple, or worse, or on the back, then follow the treatment of what lies in front; if it's large, use sewing; and if small, apply powder; and if it's deep into the bone, and there are splinters, if you treat the wound and remove all foreign objects; and if they're not removed, leave the wound to heal naturally, to aid in extractions; and for other wounds on other members, make judgments as we have stated.
dou derrompement dou ventre	about the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Laparotomies are large, medium, and small; from a major wound there might be any number of times the intestines or parts of the intestines come out, through which foreign objects enter. And sewing is more difficult, and never surpasses a minor wound compared to a major one, because when you attempt to reintroduce the intestines, they do not go in as far, for they swell whenever they feel cold; therefore, it's better to treat smaller wounds, so that we can properly reintroduce the intestines in their place. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: The two common stitches occur during the laparotomy of the abdomen, and the stitches of other body injuries and two other specific stitches are common with other wounds; yet all these are more suitable with the laparotomy stitches, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines has been exposed, and it's easy to replace what's injured, this can be done through one of two methods: either by taking advantage of the size of the wound as we have explained or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: wet a sponge or immerse half of a linen cloth in just water, or you can boil it with vinegar and cypress and needles, and immerse the intestine until the warmth expands; and after doing these things repeatedly, let it cool to help reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or boiled and seasoned (cooked) broth, because through this it becomes easier to enter with little else; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision on the tool that one uses for empyting urine; and your first treatment is cooled so that the cut remains, as we do not cut without great necessity; and these are the tools to split: if you cut inside at the curve and outside non, then visualize this shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, if you can place it back according to its natural form in its proper location, do so, for this is worth trying.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is extensive, and it's located on the lower abdomen, you should have the patient lie with their back towards the sky, and place their legs higher than their head. And if it's in the part below the belly, then position their head and buttocks higher than the abdominal parts; similarly, when dealing with a wound at one of the two parts of the abdomen, ensure that the lower section is above the other. In this manner, you should carry out what I say about large and smaller wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use whatever you are equipped with; then take hold of all the edges of the wound and gather them in your hands, and bind all along the tear with thread, then stitch them together; this is the common way of suturing. You should choose a needle or needles, depending on the size of the wound's width; leave about half an inch from the edge of the wound before you begin stitching; place the needle where it suits you, using sturdy thread, and pierce through both layers of skin with the thread; then pierce through both layers of flesh inside the skin until you've reached that part, stitch together the two ends of the flesh in three places; then sew a double strand of thread around each end of the needle, then stitch along the edges of the wound, leaving about half an inch between each stitch; then sew a second stitch following the same process as the first one; and keep doing this until all of the wound is stitched up; choose needles that are neither too fine nor too thick; because very fine needles can cut through the flesh, while overly large ones don't fit well into it: you should choose middling-sized needles. Don't stitch them too close to the skin or the leather where they might cut open the wound before suturing. Then smooth out the ends of the needles so they won't irritate the patient at night; and cover them with cloth or bandages while keeping the stitches in place until the wound has healed completely; this method of stitching with needles is more practical for small wounds as you can use one needle for two consecutive stitches, commonly, where you gather together both layers of skin and both layers of flesh in one needle when it's followed by a sturdy thread midway. When you have pierced all four ends together, pull the needle back to where you started, doing this like tying knots; leave about half an inch between each stitch; this stitching heals the body, and I stitched a wound once on someone whose belly was torn open with a knife, which was more than a palm wide, and contained intestines that were also several palms long, and it was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestines when they had been away for twenty-four hours and the wound was healed up to fifteen days. I treated him and he became well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when they thought he would die, it was a miracle; and I didn't treat him with any ointment. I was in the area where one couldn't find oil or any medicine, so I used no medicines. Instead, I put old cotton twice a day on his wound and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing: take the needle and place it from the outer side until it enters within; when it pierces straight through the flesh, sew along where you have inserted the needle or where it has pierced, and then make another piercing from the inner side to the outer side. The principle of this sewing is that you stitch like a marten furs, leaving one end free on one side and then picking up again on the other, until the entire seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suture, as Gallienius correctly states, is like what no one does, which unites the two parts naturally together, and places one tip of thread near to the other tip, in this manner: make a needle or thread akin to a thorn pierce only that part, then leave the two tips on the thread; then turn the needle, and have it pierce through from underneath to inside under both tips, at the points where the two tips are. Then have the needle pierce each of them from underneath to inside through other two threads akin to a thorn belonging to the opposite side; and this is the standard method of suture and most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens said this word, and no one attests to it, that we should stitch the abdomen with two needles, or there be thread in each; and you must push one needle from one side, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew corroies. And know that when the wound is halfway through the belly, this stitch feels heavier than any others on his or her belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, just like when the surgeon has cleaned it out, place everything back in its proper position, then apply a poultice. If the surgeon has already cleaned out the wound, apply nothing else until the wound begins to heal; clean with string, sew up the sutures and stitches, and care for the wound as you would others until it heals completely; if you have no medicines, when it starts to heal, use old cotton, then stir it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine for many kinds of wounds; and if you suspect that the wound might lead to infection in major parts of the body, then it is necessary for you to soak light woolen bandages in oil heated with heat or rose oil, and place them between the joints, and remove them from behind. And when there is pain or gangrene at the edges, which happens often, then catheterize with black wine, and similarly if gangrene reaches up to the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that for large intestines it heals more easily than small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is named 'young' cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the obstruction of veins that are present there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approach of its nature towards nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the liver jumps out of the wound, then reset it back in the same way as an intestine when it's fresh; and if it is old and turned to a reddish or black color, it is necessary that you tie up the part which is black so that no blood flows from there because there are veins and arteries. Then cut off what lies between this tie-off point, and hang both ends under the area of the wound until outside beyond for easing the extraction when the liver stops bleeding, and then treat the wound.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can try to restore it in certain ways, because I have seen that someone was pierced by a lance or had stomach wounds; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became ulcerated and turned into an fistula, with its waste product emission and gaseous passage; I treated it according to what I could manage, and continued to refine until it healed properly, and sewed up the intestines.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it join, I doubted that the patient might have pain in his stomach; and there was no harm, but remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and reported to any experimenters that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner: take large-tusked oxen, then bring together the edges of the wound. And when the oxen's mouth has opened, put them on the two edges, if she forces her mouth upwards; and then close the head, and it stays so that it cannot be released, then place another ox after in this manner as before, until the entire wound is covered; and thus keep the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	For the ones who get inflamed in the intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, they can tie the intestine with a delicate thread cut from an animal's intestine, like this: take the tip of that intestine thread which has become quite thin, then tie it onto another thread made of fine linen, then thread the needle with this thread and sew the intestine, then set the wound stitches while pulling them tight; and this way of sewing with oxen is only according to the path of hope and expectation; and if there's a large and broad wound, especially when it's in one of the intestinal loops, as long as no obstruction or damage exists, because of its intricacy.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula, or where it might be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, as it matures, is universally termed 'fistula', and similarly when it becomes covered with hair and hardens.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodulation that becomes hard and white, or one does not feel pain, and it also grows hair like a bird's feather; and sometimes it is clear and hollow inside, and at other times thick; sometimes small, and at other times quite large; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that isn't healed, and there is no pus, leaves only through one of the eight causes: namely, due to the smallness of blood or pus; or because of its malevolence; or because there is hard pus inside and on the skin, which does not allow pus to form; or there is too much bone; or the flesh is rotten, and the material has a bad quality; or the medicine used in treatment was poor; or due to the manner in which corruption resembles pestilence; or due to the property of digestion being slow, leading to delayed health, and expelled naturally; or there are veins or bones present: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and treatments with medicine, within this division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistula, which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body. For there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, either at the base or inside organs like stomachs, bladders, or any part of the torso, back spine, or within joints of hands or feet; and if they affect the primary function of a limb's main structure and resemble it.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are problematic for healing. There is no other reason but ignorance; if there exists any fistula that does not reach to where I have said and you attempt its cure, and you perceive it clearly, use an arachnid or iron tent, if the fistula is straight then use it; if the fistula is twisted, use a subtle plumb line instead because plumbs bend along the twists. If you cannot find the exact location of the twisted fistula by using tents, then catheterize through one of its twisted parts, for moisture spreads from one twist to another; and cleanse afterwards, and carefully remove any bone or nerve that might be there, asking the patient about their pain when you press with your hand. Note where they feel it; and once you truly know the location, if not in relation to a joint, a nerve, an artery, a vein, or anywhere else I've mentioned, follow what I have instructed: remove the pus and rotten matter inside; then cure until it is healed. If the fistula is deeply embedded straight through, make your cut as deep as possible, then use moistened tents in medicine juice and apply them up to the head of the fistula until the medicine dissolves the remaining excesses; then cover with healing ointment for as long as it takes to heal completely. If not healed by this method, cauterize as we have described before, if the bone has been corrupted by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve is injured and the main limbs are harmed, as we have said; and if an os (bone) is exposed, and there's decay and darkness, you should operate until all decay has been removed. Then cleanse with antiseptic things until it's healed; and if it hasn't healed, proceed again as before. Know that this procedure only goes so far: keep uncovering and cleaning until you reach the bottom, removing all decay; then restore the bone; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not so, know that the corruption is too deep, you cannot bring it forward; should there be no other option but to leave it to nature. And if there's a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with tongs, take it out with an appropriate instrument suitable for this task. If there are many bones, extract them all, do not leave any one of them. And if moisture is against your will, and there is no fear or danger, then fight with the moisture, and remove flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something to promote putrefaction on the wound instead. Leave it until the muscles have completely rotted inside the bones. Then they will disintegrate more easily. If it's a large bone like from a leg or thigh, only let decay occur as long as all of that part is rotten. Then heal the wound. And if there is much putrefied matter reaching up to the bone; you should remove and cover everything up to the point of decay, then treat until it heals over. And I will tell you about a case where an abscess appeared in a man's leg from which you can take example and help for your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man in his XXXth year, who had pain in his leg due to something originating inside the body that spread until it reached the leg. There emerged a large abscess, and there wasn't any reason for opening it outwardly; but surgeons operating by their folly opened far enough so that the pus was released through them, and they ate away much of the tissues, turning into a fistula, and there came off an immense amount of pus that made the whole body swell with heat and body fluids. And many doctors kept treating him for II years, and none knew anything about the art of surgery until I was summoned, examined his leg and the medicines used to treat it, and what ate away through the open wounds extensively. It turned the parts of the body red from youthfulness, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these depressions, and then searched all the depressions, finding that some came against each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurriedly did so and found one of the depressions where I discovered a part of the bone. I found that it was corrupted and pitted, and the corruption reached inside the bone; it appeared to me that there was no other corruption than what I removed; then I began to heal the wound with medicine for a long time, but could not stitch it together; and then I continued, discovering the bone as before, finding that the corruption had continued in the bone, which I discovered, and then removed it. I aimed to stitch up the wound, but I only stitched together within a palm of the bone, and pulled it back to its full length, then replastered it with medicine; and it healed quickly and was sewn together, and did not need to be restarted for the operation, due to his weakness from illness and fear of death that I had.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the case of blood loss, it often happens, but was completely cured. Bone grew instead at its place, and it had a hard texture, with good disposition and no harm or adverse effect from all sides, neither outward nor inward.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, should this happen: take hold and pull at the end of the bone that is open, and command that it be extended upwards; then tie another piece of larger cloth than the first one you took, and tie it around the flesh which is inside the bone, stretching the ends, so as to pull out the rotten flesh underneath, revealing the flesh on the surface where you want to heal, ensuring not to injure the flesh; place a stick or board under the bone to cover over the rotten flesh; do the healing several times until the corruption can be seen and felt, and heal again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone has been corrupted and does not open, and if the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, remove all the flesh. Then put the charcoal nearby, then let the corruption extend from one side to another, and keep the corruption for as long as you can, just like what we've said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut through the corrupted joint, and expose the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, there should be no angle except that which should be cut; and if the corruption is either one of the hand’s fingers or foot’s toes, it becomes very hard but still you must investigate this corrosion according to how it opens. Clean up all ways possible from this process without opposing the vein or nerve; know that the incision and instruments for cutting these bones are many depending on the shape and appearance of the bone, its size and subtlety, its grandeur and smallness, and its hardness; so each form of operation should have its instrument according to their likeness; know also that practice will show you the tool you need based on knowledge of this art, and testimony from various diseases' presentations; indeed, if you think about what tool is needed according to how it suits.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints suffer either due to internal causes or external ones; and when you have treated that corrosion with medicine therapy and found no improvement, it is necessary to cover that limb up until the point where the corrosion occurs, so that the maladies escape via this death or through malice which is greater than the fault of the limb; and signs are such that limbs turn black, as if scorched by fire, and after turning black, since the corruption spreads from member to member, it takes over everywhere in the body. If you rush to cover it up, and if it's due to the impact of some venomous animal like a sea scorpion or snake and such, when corrosion is on the head of the two legs, then cover it up, and don't give it space till reaching the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.
