Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the symptoms of the onset of this vein are such that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the blood changes, and the vein begins to protrude, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And when the shoulder has been opened, it must be that you wrap inside with a piece of leather about three-quarters to two-thirds, and tie it, leaving the leather hanging on the leg. And every time there is a need for more, if you cover again with the leather and tie it; and if it's too long, if you cut off a part, cover it back up, and don't trim its root until it's fully out. For if you cut it, it enters into flesh, brings on pus and decay or necrosis in the vicinity, and worsens illness. And for this thing, it must be treated little by little till completion, without leaving anything out; and there is no time when this vein after being treated to five palms long, or ten, and a hand more than me, which was from ten palms long, that when you cover it, if it lasts one or two days, then pierce it until the bottom so all discharges, and empty the contents within, and apply antiseptic medicines for several days, then proceed to cure as for abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never at this vein with cold hands, and equally when it opens in the joint of the foot, or of the foot, where a lot of loss occurs, and where there are cold hands; so then treat accordingly as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	The verses that spring up between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often afflicts cows, and it's a small worm that grows between the skin and muscle, and travels throughout the body, up and down. You can feel its presence from member to member until it reaches the skin where it was going, causing pain; and it is infested with putrefaction from various fluids, such as worms, snakes, maggots and roundworms in the stomach; one cannot determine its severity, because when it travels through the body, and goes up to the head, and arrives at the eye, by chance enters, destroys the eye; this happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one can only say when it is going: henceforth then you must tie the arm up above and below with a strong rope tightly bound, then cut upwards, force treatment, and if there is not enough fluid in the wound, if it needs to be cauterized with fire, until it stops bleeding; and the greater nuisances it causes are when they flow into the eye, as we have said. And if you see it coming or head close to the eye, then bind tightly under it the eyelid formation, cut upwards, force treatment; and it is necessary to use the aid of purification of body with medicines that dissolve for the evils of humors released, and beware of eating diseased meat causing corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain which comes from wind congestion
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it's a pain that occurs in any limbs, and spreads from limb to limb; I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to treat a woman who felt ill, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm. And shortly after, I saw it rise up as if a worm was climbing towards her shoulder, quicker than anything else, just like quick silver when cut from one thing to another; the pain left that place, and settled into her shoulder, then soon spread throughout her body, until it reached her other arm; afterwards she told me that it twisted inside her body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was marveling greatly how she moved from member to member in such a way, for I had never witnessed this disease in such manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	In any case, I wanted to mention that many wish for the pain in one place to move to another, but I did not want it like what I saw in the woman; and I thought it was due to her hot body, with exposed veins, and due to this constraint, the wind's pressure becomes apparent; and none perceive according to this reason among those who are delicious, and have moist bodies and restored veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, do this: press it immediately above and below quickly, then press until the wind pressure leaving the body; and cauterize the body; and if you don't see it at your fingers, treat the one who debouts the wind pressure, such as stinking pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity among them is that some have large points, and small ones, and those that are hooked, or soldered together; and there are arrows with two angles, and others with tongues, and those that have pieces; and this kind defecates in any member according to two manners: either in a primary body part like the head, as for example the brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, or similar parts.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes to the shoulder, in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appear: so it is necessary that you be prepared for the removal of this arrow, because death follows in various stages; and when this ill sign does not appear and the arrow has not been fully removed, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow penetrates and punctures the bone, and jumps over a certain distance that is above the brain, is when blindness and deafness occur together with dizziness and fever, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and reddening of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the intellect, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it lacks strength from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it loses speech and voice; and a white moist flow coming out from the wound that resembles pus, and also burns like burnt meat; and if these signs appear, then take them seriously and remove the arrow if it isn't already.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the wart when it shrinks or changes into a heart shape indicates that it is close to the left breast. It also feels like being stuck in something solid, not empty; and sometimes the wart behaves like a pulse, with black blood coming out, and coldness, sweat, and fainting: know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never pierces is that bubbles do not jump out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with coldness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow stops in the thigh's covering, it pierces the small bones; and causes great pain and severe suffering and sighing; and moves all limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow stops in or near the stomach, by chance it jumps out of the wound with any undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow stops in or near the stomach or abdomen, and it jumps out without any meat passing through the intestine, there is no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow stops in the bladder, and the urine jumps out, causing severe pain for the patient: you should know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and the neck and the throat and the shoulder blade and the auxiliary (shoulder) bone and the spine in the back and the ribcage and the hip bones and the legs, and resembling limbs, are protected according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it's not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one house where an arrow had struck him in the neck at the base of his nose: I tried it and pulled it out from the other side under the ear fat, and found no difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And pulled out an arrow from a game that had struck him in the ear fat under the paper skin, and the arrow was still inside, unable to reach anything but its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow length without any weight loss; the game was found easy, and it caused no harm.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And extract an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and it was the Arabic arrow in the ears: I would pull out the stubble hairs, and with as much subtlety as possible while pulling it, made the Christian whole again.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And extract an arrow from his home, which was stuck in the chest or belly, and I thought he would die; but after having passed thirty days, if it didn't change its position; I cut into the arrow, removed it, and then pulled it out without any bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see the home to which an arrow has fallen or landed on its back, and found the wound healed from within; and remained the arrow inside it, without altering its natural positions, nor caused harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And there's another man who was hit by an arrow on his face and had the wound stitched up; and ever since he has suffered great pain; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And he was struck by an arrow at the home of princes' king, who had it stuck in his nose and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was completely stuck. I was summoned for treatment after it stayed there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried everything with a subtle technique and did not feel it; and there was pain and discomfort around his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed a healing plaster on his left side that was absorbing and digestive because his ears were not inflamed; and revealed the arrow's position in the ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the dressing to his hands on that day, and healed the wound quickly. He then stayed in bed for a long time after, until he felt the arrow inside his nose for one full day; and I told him this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed corrosive mercury medicine on the wound daily until it opened, then tried it and felt the tip of the arrow as it emerged from its place; after that I adjusted in the opening of the wound with this corrosive mercury medicine, until the head of the arrow became visibly evident to me. The ends remained closed for about four months, but eventually the wound healed so well that I could use forceps and operate on both sides, unable to pull them out; then I continued to refine and invent ways of instruments, until I successfully used forceps made properly in one day, as described in this section at the end of the chapter. After that, when I handled the wound with these forceps according to its form, it healed completely without any issues.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and if the wound is sealed, and if the patient recovers completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I told you about the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that when you apply your treatment to what I don't mention, because books can't encompass everything; but the wise masters compare on quite a few small things, and on what is present and lacking, find new works, and new instruments, for the removal of foreign matters which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows penetrate members where they are inserted according to two manners: either through their side or they enter; and if it enters or goes in when it's pierced from its side, this is an arrow entering into its flesh, and it never occurs now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it be until the char remains intact internally, and the issue appears; similarly, if it is stuck in bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for a few days, removing each day; then it will jump. If it doesn't jump, poke through entirely with a fine needle until the tendons are enlarged internally, and then remove them.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and reaches up to one of the brain's cavities, or any other incident as I've described to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but leave it until it becomes even after a few days, because if the arrow comes up to the sinus, it means death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not reach up to the sinus, and the patient remains well for any number of days without any bad incident, then prepare for removal.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's firmly stuck in that way and cannot come out by itself, then you should apply arrows internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to its original position within the body so that it cannot be seen by touch alone, take care in examining every part of it; and if you feel it with your hand without any suitable instrument at hand; and if you cannot reach due to the size of the wound or depth of the arrow and there are no bones, nerves or veins present, cut as wide as necessary so that you can pull out the arrow. If you can grab a part of the shaft when pulling the arrow, remove the flesh around it until it falls off cleanly, then bend or break the ears of the arrow as much as possible to allow easier removal; and be careful not to break the arrow but rather pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one attempt, until the shoulder is properly aligned within its socket, then move it. For the extraction process is made easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding prevents you from doing as we have advised in treating it in this chapter, then follow what has been said about treatment; and guard against cutting near nerves or vessels, and position yourself so that with care you can remove the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to how they were before the arrow hit them, because that is the best way; if you cannot do this, then have them positioned as indicated by their symptoms show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from the other side, or if it exposes something from it, or if there is an swelling in the place where you can see or feel it distinctly: then cut upwards as high as your scissors can take hold, and then press: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it's held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it doesn't want to come out, leave it still and start the extraction again until it does; and if there is an arrow inside her, push it all along; and if she's at the tip of the arrow, once you have administered pushing, if you administer the tool with a point, so that the arrow's point goes into the handle of the tool; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is caught by the tool, when administering the tool to the point entering, in order to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is encased, it is necessary for you to hold all the flesh around where I am entering or have entered, if possible, then treat the wound as is proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits the hand or arm or stomach or bladder or ribs and is close by, you can cover it up if possible; and make sure not to cover the vein and nerves. Then extract it, then suture the wound when necessary; and treat until the wound heals.

des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins similar to those common ones
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins through which we bleed, from which are sixteen heads: namely, two small ones behind the ears, called "hair veins"; and the two arteries in the two visible temples; and two veins that are within the eyelids of the two eyes, known as "sucking veins"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is on the head near the nose; and the two jugulars located at the neck; and the two veins above the mouth in the lips, these are known as "lip veins"; and two veins under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated are in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it is found on the left side of the body, and people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called 'fascial', composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein if it's on the right or left side of the body, and people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the ulna, and this is the one that is treated, which clearly opens externally on the stomach.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The salve table is the vein that's between the index finger and the ring finger, and it has two layers; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is below the bend of the wrist on the left side of the body, and the second is sophene which is at the ankle on the right side of the body; and the vein that's called "ness", that's in the ankle on the other side. In the other leg, there are three veins under these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	Surgical treatments for veins located behind the ears were conducted by ancient cathar surgeons and also to relieve migraine; understanding the qualities of a surgeon as I have explained, concerning this, you should feel under your head where the maladies exist, rub it or the vein area with one harsh cloth; then tighten the malady's neck into a twist until each two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent from the head: then press on and when you feel the pulse underneath your head, indicate to them; then take the lancet and hold the blade at the vein down towards the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards, cut through it carefully and the skin as two inches wide, and make blood come out until you see it; then pull and tie it tightly till it heals; and I have already discussed the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The treatment of the two arteries located in two temples, if it is ancient and stable, as well as to the use of old remedies for eye diseases; and the quality of a surgeon should be such as I describe: and that the patient restrains his neck until both vessels are clearly visible; and feels the pulse on your right, then raises your head slightly; then press your hand over the artery near your right index, and hold the lancet there, then raise the artery upwards near you, and seal it, in the same way as with other arteries, and follow the bleeding according to necessity; then release the patient, place your thumb on the artery for an hour, then put cotton on top; and after that form the bandage and leave it until it heals completely. And we have spoken about their extraction and operation, or where this book starts.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The treatment of the vein above the forehead is as valuable as that of the cephalic vein in diseases affecting the face, and for migraines, and for redness; and the quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears. And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, allowing blood to flow according to the amount you see; then untwist for the patient his neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy and there is no risk of a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz. The treatment for the two veins located in the eyes and nose, as well as redness, and ear inflammation within the ear, and diseases affecting the face; and the quality of their treatment is that the patient twists his neck due to some cause, as described before. Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is thin, perchance it breaks; then make it correspond to blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The treatment for nosebleeds from the head area involves using water and salt, as well as various remedies for face illnesses like migraine and fever that come with it, and especially when the face is old; and the quality of this treatment consists in forcing your nostrils up by squeezing them with your left hand, then taking a long fine flame, and inserting it between the two nasal cavities, because the nose does not open well, and now the blood will start to flow; do not allow too much heat, adjust the bleeding gently according to your need, then let it rest for a night as it is quickly restored; this is the shape of the flame:

de la sainie des leivres	On the healing of the wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The surgery for veins above affects the mouth and causes gum decay, and cuts in lips, and nosebleeds and inner cheeks.

Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres. Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it sticking up as high as a child's urine stream, and the veins are red and subtle, you should know that this is from an artery: so hurry, place your finger for some time then remove it when the bleeding stops, just as many times happens; hold the arm still, and leave him alone, don't move the patient at all until they're alright; be cautious, and don't move them until they are sound.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans. Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of ginger, and cut it, then take one half and bind well up to the other side; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, treat as we have said, with powders that stop blood loss; and for the minor treatment of wounds, and the strength in holding the arm steady, these bandaging methods are not greatly varied due to the small size of the wound, and the power in keeping the arm still.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The treatment of the vein among its parts heals blood from the head above and the heart below because it consists of the basilica and cephalic components as we have mentioned, and requires that the healer be aware of the nerve nearby, and if he doesn't go far enough down, and finds the nerve, and swells and the health is damaged, possibly leading to inability to heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it doesn't open in any individuals due to its intricacy, then you should treat its origin with the instrument; and avoid touching the nerve using your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.

Always aim for the lightest option, and don't be discouraged if it needs to be done twice; and sometimes swell some limbs in certain individuals when doing it the first time, but there is no harm in that.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of treatment depends on your thought or consideration.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about hygiene is that it is managed solely for the purpose of maintaining health and avoiding future illnesses; and one should perform hygiene in any of the three arteries: namely, cephalic (head), faste (lower body) and basilic (arm); and one should wash at the beginning of prayers on your knees, in autumn and after winter meals when signs of fullness appear; and you should wash on the first or third day, after two hours or up to three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Hygiene against diseases does not have a fixed time, but only when the need arises during the day or after meals, at any hour and in all circumstances; it is not advisable to wash children up to 14 years old, nor pregnant women until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	No one who has surpassed sixty years of age should undergo surgery.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone seeks to heal themselves, in whatever manner that might be, it is necessary for them to purge their intestines with a light cathartic if they have held back food, so that the veins do not draw excesses from the intestines that harm the main limbs; nor will one recover someone who has been too overfed by meat or drunkenness, until such time as they are strong and unill. If there is a warning about healing after colic pain, vomiting, abdominal cramping, frequent urination, or labor pains, as well as staying awake and fasting, and the like, then it is to refine blood and help heal from below the third part of the backside; then avoid work, pinching, excesses, and similar activities. And be restrained and joyful, have healing higher than that which heals you, rub your wrists twice or three times, then pinch your tie somewhat from above because if it's too tight or loose, it can't correct the intestines. And then rub their limbs with a bit of old olive oil, then place your left hand's finger on the vein under your back for a little where you wish to heal, so that the vein does not burn and fail at being pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like strings when heated, and there are some that are full of windiness, so that when one places them over the flame, they retract from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus belong to those kinds; and if it causes the vein to inflame, then the wound is too narrow, because in such cases the surgeons should be knowledgeable about these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it's good; and if not, it should be tried again slightly near that place or on the skin quickly, when the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limbs are swollen and the patient feels hot and feverish, let him rest for one or two days and do not bind his arm: perhaps an abscess will appear; don't bathe or immerse him afterwards, then begin to bleed again as he wishes. des sainies de ventouse	of suction healings
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or spiders, or leeches; and blood extraction is done in two ways: by piercing and drawing out blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction process which can cause injury is done in two ways: either without any fire or with it; and the suction performed by causing injury and extraction of blood happens at fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely under the head; and another is under the neck; and two others are each side of the neck; and the suction below the chin; and the suction over the shoulders; and the suction over the pimples; and the suction under both arms; and the suction over both legs; and the suction over both ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, as it is from small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and because of this, it does not weaken any, as in blood-healing procedures; and it should not be administered to any disease caused by congestion, until all organs have been emptied.

And those with a cold complexion should drink honey syrup and half of an aromatic wine that's between old and new, and eat small portions, and consume small pieces of meat and young birds and pigeon; on the day they are to be suctioned, they should drink more than they eat. It is suitable for some to give them once or twice before or after suction therapy to strengthen their main body parts; make the stomach subtle but it's not suitable for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are used to cause injury are those placed on the liver and stomach, and in podagre, and on the belly and anus and kidneys and hip. For this member cannot bear injury over wounds, and one does not do it forcefully only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them around nipples when a child is born; to remove the viscosity that is within limbs, as we place suction cups around the belly and anus for reducing limb size; and removes pain where there's obstruction or stone, and by its attractive virtue unexpectedly removes obstruction, or empties the stone from its place; and thus it operates when placed on liver and stomach when there's retained excessive air, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only that; and never are they administered together with fire, and never filled with hot water as in such illnesses due to pleurisy, and in this manner one fills the suction cup with hot water or water where herbs useful for the ailment have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used for fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And have two fingers of length half a palm each side, and at its middle has one edge on the inner part halfway I slightly blunt, as for driving in a nail, it should be in front if it does not hurt the patient when putting it onto the limb; and has inside one spine like across an arachnid or iron, to place a candlestick handle, and are both large and small according to illnesses and the season of those taking them; because suction cups for children are different from adults' ones, and slimmer than fat's.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And we should place this suction cup onto the limb: take the candlewick or thread and put it through the suction cup across the spine that is inside the suction cup, ensuring light is at the bottom of the suction cup to prevent burning the patient; then place it onto the limb, keep your fingers on the blunt area as we mentioned, so when you want, if vapor comes out, remove the suction cup; and take the thread in a similar way, repeat frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup then which is administered in pleurisy disease, there is no strength nor lack thereof for any age or severity, and it is administered forcibly only when it is full of fluid, and placed solely on the body part; and this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Blistering blisters are administered only in limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and they should be treated in naked bodies like elbows or knees, and others similarly. The quality of blistering is that when you find blisters that are in mild cool water without pus, take them; then put a nut in warm water until they are familiarized, with nothing in their stomachs; and then lance the veins and apply suction cups, then rub the body until it turns red, then place the blisters on it; and when they are full, and release, if there is any area where one can place a suction cup, then put it on, for this lasts a long time afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the aid in fire and water, quite well, then smear it with essence. And if the aid recovers too soon after the dislocation process, soak a linen cloth in cold water, put it on, until the skin is dry; and if there are multiple wounds, put powdered vitriol or ash on them, until they are dry; or you can place half of peeled peas under the wound and leave them to roast against the aid, which will now stop bleeding. And if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins don't easily take, rub the aid with fresh blood or stick an awl into them until blood comes out, then put it back, and soon as they smell the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are bleeding, powder a little aloes and powdered wheat on it, or ash, and they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and for restoring fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, my dear son, that the remedies in this chapter, which are not found in any of the old books, nor have anyone ever read them; and for this reason, the knowledge has been removed from our land, because I never found any good ones; and I know nothing else, relying solely on the knowledge from the old books I studied extensively as part of my scientific work, through experimentation, and by the habit of my life; and in this chapter, I have described what is contained within it, abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are used, just like I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or introduce this book's contents and chapters where the senses apply their understanding, staying true to reality. This way, those who have experienced it will know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fractures or dislocations or twists or coldness come to any part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly cleanse the patient on both sides, without leaving anything behind, like weakness in body parts, children, or old people; if the person's strength isn't sufficient, too hot, too cold; and consume cold foods such as icy jousts, and liver and goat meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats. Do not fill your stomach with meat that fills blood vessels until you are certain there is no abscess or spreading of material within the body. If the patient recovers under their previous governance until it was used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that cause abundant nourishment, or have a viscous quality, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and chestnuts, and peas, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, among similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with this nourishment, the injuries are healed more quickly and the breaking [of bones] is overcome.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the old and the decrepit cannot be properly repaired or joined according to their nature due to the drying out of the limbs, or those as well who are too soft, such as the bones of young children; but give care, set on the broken bone I large pieces that swell up and unite the limb together, until it resists as it was before; and do not end abruptly with your work, for this needs to be fed with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures come in many different ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is breaking that would go to war, and another when sharpening, such as the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with breaking due to injury, and breaking with a small crack in its entirety.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each way it has its own tool and proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory brings to the mind; and is known that the breaking of the bone appears when the limb is twisted, opens well from outside, and feels pressing under the hand; and when there is no twisting or hitting sensation, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no breakage; but it may have twisting, or crack, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But if you cannot move it by hand, then apply the remedies that follow next, and then gently manipulate it now.

And know that the breach which went in the direction of the animal, and its two parts are detached, now they must be placed evenly as you would do with pus stains or gashes; and if pus comes out after being dressed, let it have no rest until the pus subsides; then place it even as you can lightly and carefully move it, knowing that the restoration of this is easier than in those with pieces; then squeeze it as per what follows.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, and it is divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or at your hand it's a small limb, or divided into two tendons, or one tendon at your hand; then place the limb according to its natural shape, so when the broken parts of the member are healed, you should stretch them in all directions by moving them as you can, and make sure that through your actions no injury or pain befalls the patient; and adjust both ends of the bone well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it doesn't seem to be perfectly located: if it is dressed beautifully, and not strained too much, without squeezing as those who bring out abscesses by their work do, just like we have wanted many times.

And when the limbs are in place, chastise well the patient so they do not move them, neither while awake nor asleep, neither when turning around, nor in any other manner; and ensure that the limbs are securely placed to prevent any feeling of pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when they do not feel any pain, they are not in the right position yet. It is necessary to arrange them properly so that they do not feel any pain. Ensure they are placed correctly; let no curvature come about when you restore them; and know that the quality of the broken limb follows what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are various in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And there are small limbs like arms and legs and so on: it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen. Then go above the break and tighten less so as not to move the break; gently soften the band little by little until a significant portion of the healthy side is reached; start again with another band and tie around it tightly like before; then come back just below the break area, tight it moderately neither too hard nor too soft, as we explained in the previous section. Then place linen or bandage loops between the bindings till they are evenly placed, then secure everything above the bend, and finally put on properly made pins if there is no pus or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, you should place a soothing anti-abscess substance upon it and remove the swelling, allowing it to stay this way for some days; then work on your stars (referring to acupuncture points), using needles that are half the width of a hair carefully reinserted, or from the shafts used to make acupuncture needles, or from palm leaves, fitting them according to this description.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the stars (acupuncture points) one puts on the piercing are slightly larger and wider than the others; they should also be as long as is necessary for the size of the limb, whether small or large. For if the thread is large, like some people who create their needlework with rough linen cord threads, and this is a great mistake, because the piercing cannot be uniform if it's too fine, and it doesn't suit for there to be less than two finger widths between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the limbs are bruised by the joints of the sockets after reduction in their healthy positions, then apply padding with linen or shredded wool on them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is due to piercing (or stab) injury, and the ribs are broken, I will instruct on its treatment thereafter.

For when the limbs are large, it is not appropriate to apply these plasters until after five days or seven, or longer according to your treatment in each case; and here comes the way of the ancient plastering for restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists: take flour that stands on mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick. Use it like this, and this is the common method of the restorative plaster for fixing fractures in various positions, just as well with women and young children since it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method for setting breaks and dislocations and twists: take three parts of garlic and dill and wormwood and asafetida and Arabic gum and mastic, in total. Use five parts of myrrh and aloes, also in total. Add seven parts of alechil. Grind all these into a powder, then mix them with the yolk of an egg; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster as it has a good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, proving beneficial to many people.

Another method of plastering for twisting injuries: take mugwort and valerian root, each in 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, each in 9 parts; aloe six parts; Armenian balm ten parts. Another method for bandaging joints and bones in their place, and relieving the pain that occurs, and using the bone and fracture: take new wool, and the grease in a dish with oil cooked, and place it on the joint.

Another method of plastering that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and terrestrial oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for bandaging in the restoration of bone fracture and to alleviate the exudation from the abscess.

Take root of willow herb, chamomile, violet flowers, groundnut, from each one part; and grind, mix with wine, and if the limbs are warm, mix it with wet coriander water, or water alone, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method more effective than the first one when it comes to reattachment during healing of the limb.
