Take roots of vismalve, and linseed, balmroot, melilot, and wormwood, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from all take one part; and grind and mix with saltwater, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that one should apply to the broken limb for strength restoration using a paste made of wax and oil, and nothing else, more. He says it should be neither too soft nor too hard between two states.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests one should apply to the broken limb for restoration dry things slightly warm, such as mire, aloe, incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plaster useful for injury and pain: take mussels and pigeon meat or bird feathers, and basil leaves, and equal parts of wine vinegar, grind them together, and then make a plaster with it and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then gently move it after some time, and watch so that the patient does not feel any pain or movement in his bone from its place. If you do this by hand instead of using tools. And if pain comes to the limb, or itching without rest or swelling, then rush, remove the splint, and put on a new one immediately; take light strips and wet sponge, dip them in water, and cool the limb until the itching stops and the pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then place it under dry wool, moistened with water or oil, and secure it with a bandage, as long as you are sure of preventing infection. And calm the inflammation of the limb, and relieve the pain, then start the delicate reattachment again with just a little splint, and do not apply pressure as before; and handle it delicately until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus and redness, pain and swelling are present throughout the bone, and you need to plaster and bind it, then repeat as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there is no change in the limb that we have said, or if it only gets reset after three to four or five or seven days; and never let it stay for more than twenty days, as shown, until the swelling subsides and the adjustment of the flesh comes about. Then you should hold the restraint tighter than before, and increase its meat production, just as I have said previously. And if you see that the skin has dried too much beyond what is necessary, understand that complications cannot occur; immerse it then in hot water each time you reset it, every third day, and cleanse a little of the wound; through this process, remove the pus from the limb and hasten those who do not heal properly, causing the limb to return in a distorted manner: this is bad news, and these are harmful operations, and I see nothing else other than just letting it dry naturally and opening it straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracturing
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of fractures exist, and various appearances are present. The causes are categorized; for there are fractures made from the impact of a sword, and neck fractures that reach the bone up to its junction with flesh, just below the bone, like in an animal or a staff attack; thus this type of fracture is named "haunching".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, this kind of injury is called 'absolute break'; and it refers to the wounds resulting from these two types of breaks, whether large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential striking, or crack, or from the stone itself, or impact on the stone, or other similar incidents.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a partial break, which approaches until it reaches the tissue under the bone, or above the bone, and this injury can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there's a wound that is healed within an os as delicate as hair, and the crack small, thus this fracture is named "hairline"; and if the injury is caused by striking with stone or falling or some other thing, causing the piece of bone to fall inwards, such as how candle makers make holes into candles; if there's a piece inside the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those with softer bones like the head of someone moistened by water, such as an infant's skull; and it happens through all these methods of fracture where small pieces are dislodged, like in stables; and I will speak on its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all methods of fractures through their dislocation upon them, and the examination by prodding, and through the decayed flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	Hair loss is known by those who when an osseous fragment has been revealed and rubbed together, if it exposes black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious about malaise incidents, and if you do not see any ill-omened accidents such as vomiting, loss of understanding, expansion, paleness, fever, or if the eyes start to come out and turn red, or show other symptoms in various conditions, there is no certainty that it can heal.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the bone comes to you first, and it's in winter, if you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after your arrival that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, you should remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh around the bone becomes rotten, and accidents as we've said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of bone has reached up to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut open the broken part thus: and take hold of the part of the body in pain, exposing on the bone in all ways that are possible, and with regard to the appearance of the wound as much as possible. And if bleeding occurs during exposure, or pus forms, use what is appropriate and fill the space with damp linen in oil roset; then allow the wound to rest until the pus stops forming and bleeding ceases. Then begin by removing through the bone and proceed according to two ways of work: one way involves cutting a narrow slit from behind, which results in this shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut, which is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, all sharp, and made of iron; and work with light hands, making sure not to pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and beyond piercing, you should pierce it through, ensuring that you make cuts with steady hands, not all the way through so as not to penetrate beyond the bone by mistake, and there should be a margin or circle of about an inch above the tip, preventing the tip from passing through the bone; and you should have several of them, so each touches its length of the bone, ensuring that there are tines for both sides; this is the form of the three methods of piercing.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce inside the broken bone is that you place one wick on the bone and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then put the wick elsewhere a little after, and do this throughout, then cut in between the roots of the teeth where the bone exists, and do this more subtly than you can, gently, just as we have said, till you pull the bone to your hand or to none of the instruments that you have such as pliers, forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, if it is necessary that you remove the substance that has remained from the bone to all other instruments similar to a file, but it should be more durable and more subtle than any other file; and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or no scales, then gently scrape them with the tools. Then treat the wound with coverings and treatments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this as Galien said, which is more safe; and the needle is very strong, and it's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you must expose a part of the bone where the fracture opens and moves. So when you have exposed that part, place underneath the edge of this lens-shaped incision, as depicted here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side alone, and have the part divided into two sides, so that you are cutting towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, such that you gently hit the entire bone, and be well aware of any surrounding tissue; if it is thin over the bone, then gently tap the bone, for bones can be tapped without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then after that roughness, it's necessary to remove the scales with a sharp shaver of which you should have various quantities. To administer each one as most appropriate according to the manual and the appearance of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you appear before great shavers, and then even finer ones, and don't stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and finer breaks, you must administer care according to its direction; and this matter is not resolved for whoever has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And when the wound is discovered, it should be that you take linen bandages according to the size of the wound and soak them in rosy oil, then place them on the wound. Then take another double layer of linen and soak it in wine and rosy oil, placing it above the first bandage; do this more lightly than possible so as not to weigh down the wound, then administer a further bandage from above, without applying too much force that only touches the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until any abscesses are calmed, then remove the bandages and administer medicines such as lily roots, powdered cloves, incense powder, and aristolochia, among other things. From these prepare a powder and place it on the wound, then administer further medicated powders that do not cause irritation; and be careful to keep the wound clean so that you do not leave oil behind or allow a clot to form, because when clots form on the tissue of the brain, they move about causing great harm; for when something corrosive is placed on the wound, it irritates from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care, if nothing happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fear does not come out only because of the medicine we have put on, that virtue being there, it is necessary for you to take a portion of honey and three parts of rose oil and one drachm of glue, then apply this mixture onto your skin. Then treat it in ways that fit treatments, until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts under the nose or even just one, because these are two bones; and this lower part is made of cartilage, it does not break, nor will it take to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it's necessary for you to pinch your small finger or the back of your nose and make an equal break in that part inside your index finger. Then place this break at the tip and let air out from there until your nose regains its natural shape; do this gently and watch so that the patient doesn't feel pain due to your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the area above the nose, and cannot reach the nostril from below, it should be positioned evenly to the top of a small stick that's a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, redo this procedure, and try to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day when the abscess has subsided, then pinch at the base of your nose using a piece of linen. If the break was in one part, do so here.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should apply a bundle on the other side as well, if the fracture is there too; and make them large enough to fill out the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorative requires mixing with butter, and turning each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I don't think it's quite right, but they should be made moist in the preparation of a mixture with an egg and powder from the mill; then leave the fabric, until the bone is hard and the cartilage toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one uses goose feathers instead of tents, and if it's mixed with one egg white, and if there is a wind, and the air goes among them; then do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear near the nose as you do them, then put wadding or moistened cotton in oil of rose, or a pinch of salt.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses occur without it happening, you should apply plaster outside, made of sifted charcoal and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk. Then place them on light bandages, do not tie too tight; and if the pieces break off easily by touching the nails, and they break into small pieces, then use suitable instruments for this purpose, then cut along the wound and treat all rotten parts, by joining together, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this. And if there is no wound inside the nail, you should treat the fabric; and you put on garlic leaves until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured internally and there is no external wound,
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the fracture is in the right part, you bend your index finger into the patient's mouth towards the side of the injury. And if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then bend your index finger of the right hand towards it, and gently apply pressure on the fracture internally, and perform this action with the other hand externally, making sure to do so evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is separated into two parts, then it's necessary to administer an extension for each part until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or rupture, then restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk. Place it on the broken mandible and place one double piece of cloth; and put another large tent on the cloth well made, or an equal piece of leather long and wide according to the length of the mandible, and bind it up as tight as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, let it shift to its position on the third day and then adjust what has changed; cover with plaster, using powder from a mill combined with plenty of egg or ground oyster flour after removing the bandage; place a layer of wool on top, and when the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition doesn't change, let it be until they recover. Many times recovery occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus-filled sores appear, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture combined with a wound, it's rewarded by none of the bone being extracted; if the extraction requires instruments suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is nothing left, if the wound is wide, place one layer of plasters suitable for it to accelerate healing until it heals.
de la forcele	By the power.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strength breaks many times before, around the shoulder, and the breaking happens in three ways: when it breaks and divides into two parts, with fragments, and is easier to restore; or when there's a break accompanied by an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatments are as follows when there's breaking without an injury, where you have two assistants, so one marks the shoulder that feels the broken strength; and the other stretches up to the neck towards the affected area; then equalize the break with your hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there's no visible or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, then place a round piece of cloth or wool under the shoulder towards the body; and make it as large as your need requires; stretch and lift the strength, hold the sphere in your hand so that you can equalize the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the strength away from the front due to its presence in front, it is necessary that the patient lie with their face towards their shoulder and place a half-collar under the shoulder. Then you should press the shoulder down, while supporting it, until the bone of the strength is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then use the break at your hands, and if you find debris there, it is necessary that you cut it up; and gently pull the pieces, and if the bone cannot join through any pressure, cut into one of the incisions you have made. But place this instrument on the strength, to prevent fluid from flowing out:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And seems like a spoon, and is not found anywhere, and it should be as wide as you need, according to the size of the bone and the power of your work; and has two heads, as you see, and one is broad, and the other is narrow, just like the opening of the wound that you have made when you have treated the bones; and when you are sure about extracting the contents, if it disturbs the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt about extracting the contents properly, if you cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if there is pus being extracted, then moisten it with oil, rose water and honey, and place it on the affected area.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The process of bone dressing when it involves wounds and size, is as follows: you place on the bone a plaster made from the powder ground by the mill and some yolk of egg, then lay light bandages over it. If needed, put a ball under the wound area. Then take a very long bandage about one palm wide, cover the bandages with two layers of bandage, and then apply the plaster on top. Next, take a slender rod three fingers wide and long, wrap it around the bandage so that the edge of the bandage hangs down, making sure to keep the bandage at this height. Put the rod over the wound area, and secure the bandage at the neck. The bandage should be kept tight until the wound area is clean from both sides and you can clearly see that the rod isn't moving upwards on the broken bone. Then reapply the bandage each day, and when all threads are cut, keep restraining it. Make sure the wound heals properly by having the patient lie with a pillow under their shoulder to lift the weight off of the shoulder blade, which reduces the strain on the injured area. If you need to immobilize the arm at the neck due to potential bad accidents, do so for up to 20 days after which you can resume normal activities as long as the wound heals well within this time frame; for some people it may take up to 28 days and less than that for others.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	A fracture occurs when the shoulder breaks or is extensively torn, and this happens only upon impact; if you align it according to the shape of the breakage, then reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways possible; then apply powdered flour from the mill with plenty of eggs, and make light bandages, and place them on both sides; then put a wide but fine stick slightly wider than the shoulder, where there is no movement at any part of the shoulder, so fill that space with linen threads, so that the stick fits evenly; and then tighten it into one large bandage tightly, so that the stick does not move from its place, and check the join each day; and every time when it loosens, you tighten it, and make sure the stick is still secure if it has moved from its place, and place the patient on their side; and the shoulder is recovered in twenty days or twenty-five. And once this number of days are fulfilled, you remove the brace, and be certain, for it's not bone that comes together lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone piece sticks out before, and there's no opening in the skin, then cut it open and operate on the bone as we've instructed in handling injuries to the thigh for soothing abscesses.
de la brisure dou pis	On the breaking of the heel
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bones are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but they often break at the end.

And the restoration should be such that the body lies on its back and you place one and a half cushions between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of two ribs with your hands, and delicately put them equal in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then lay bandages and wadding above the delicate salt draft or another lightweight substance, and wrap it tightly with a blanket, and fix it to the broken bone so that it doesn't move; and turn the bandage around the back smoothly, and compress it evenly, and reward each hour the injured person, and if it heals, then tighten; and if it needs to be released due to corrosion or itching in the body, or pain or abscess, you should act quickly, release it, remove the bandages, and treat the one who has come seeking remedies in ways of treatment; then replace the bandage again and compress until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of bone fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that are between the knife and the shoulder cap, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to either of two methods: where one would take a full rod of medium thickness, as per this shape:

Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie. And if pus comes out, do not tighten for more than seven days, and place it on greased wool in a comfortable position and in oil rose; until the pus coming out is relieved. Then hold tight, using this method of holding: you should put the plaster on the wound, then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and apply the cloth, tighten it both on the shoulder joint and on the arm, so that the arm rests in its natural position, without any obstruction, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use braces, and place an extra large and strong brace above the wound, keeping one inch of space between each brace. Each brace should be so wide that it passes three inches on either side of the wound; then hold tight with these braces, as I explained at the beginning of this chapter about the wound, more firmly and not by pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the base of the nails and constriction, as we have said, at the time when you are restoring the broken member, and you doubt about discharging pus, if you leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine each three days the bandage, so that itching does not spread in the area or comes to the body because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such incidents occur, or if it isn't released until three days or later, and the patient lies with the illness on his back, having his hands on his stomach; then place under the shoulder one blanket of equal wool evenly. Examine each hour for a day or for food time, so that the shape of the broken member doesn't move, or that the bindings aren't softened; if the address by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have already placed, in such manner that the meat is at first tender; and when it begins to regain strength, then make it firm.

Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly or constricted, it should be held for dislocation for 1 day or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	"Of the breaking of the arm"
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the pair 'foscile'. One bone is small, and it's this one that covers the elbow; and the other bone is large, and it's this one that lies underneath, towards the little finger. By chance, only the larger foscile breaks or both could break, or they might come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is lighter and more successful, and the healing. And when large bones are broken, the healing goes badly, and it's worse than if they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, then it's appropriate to gently extend it slightly and put them in alignment.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large bone that is broken, then it's appropriate to pull more strongly; and extend it on the first rib, and lift the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the other fingers, and let the ribs cross themselves, with the first rib in front of him higher, so that the body doesn't suffer any pain; then extend the attendant's arm to the part above his hand or elbow, and another attendant at the other one on top.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the eyes evenly, according to their best form.

And if during the breaking into pieces, you place each in its place, and if there is none that sticks to the bone when you grasp it, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do on and with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if during the healing process, I mentioned it in a separate chapter; if take the treatment.

And apply the wax, and place the plaster of ground powder mixed with plenty of egg, then insert the needles. The threads used for stitches should be made from linen, not too thick and not too thin, as we have mentioned.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And after a few days, restore the member and the connection.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad events come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary for you to immerse the member in hot water, until that itchness is alleviated; and leave the member not moved to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the tightening, and if the ligaments have been destroyed and the bones are exposed, as seems appropriate.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no stiffness comes to the member, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it by rubbing, and let it rest for a few days, until the stiffness passes, and then tighten it again.

ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus. de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You should know that on the back of the hand and around our thumbs there are few injuries, and it only causes many plagues.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin. Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois. de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken foot

And if it happens, set it free, and address whatever comes up, just as we have said many times. de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman's body are broken, have her lie with widened hips, then tilt her towards the back part of her waist and hold her by her rear. Then fill the natural cavity in her body with cotton stuffing to the same size as she is; and place some of this inside her as well. Next, help the woman stand up slowly while lifting her back a little at a time, until the cotton comes out till it reaches the opening of nature and pushes the bones together again with her strength. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, after which she should return to normal; do this for seven or more days: then the break will be restored. If you want to observe it closely, take a goat bladder and tie a stick at its neck and fill the whole bladder into nature; then blow air into the stick until the bladder inflates internally; nature will heal the break. Then fill it with cotton again and leave her like this for some days until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.
