Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And breaking signifies more than multiple ways of restoring the correct path of restoration: hence, understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of the penis if it is broken, take a goose’s throat and fill the penis with it; then wrap bandages around it, and let it be for three days or as long as needed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	From fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the person with a fracture that also has a wound, even if it's large, like in the case of bones in the elbow or shoulder or similar, to be now cleaned, so that the cleanings which we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, you can fumigate it with vitriol (sulfuric acid), and if you don't have anything else, then start restoring the fracture in that same hour or day; or when abscesses do not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscesses start appearing, let the restoration continue for another day or two, until the abscess subsides, and don't touch it on the third or fourth day, because you might provoke a harmful incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if bone is broken and visible at the site of the open wound, it is necessary to place your hands on it gently, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not present for you to align evenly with your hands, take this iron instrument that is made of steel, which is seven inches or six inches long, and the width should match the size of the wound; and for this purpose, the surgeon must choose three or four (depending on what he needs for each treatment of bone fracture), and it should be round and a bit large so that it doesn't bend under compression against your limb during surgery, and it should have points at the front, and be thick in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche" because it requires that the curved heads be placed on the tip of the visible bone; and it should be struck once, until it heals, and be equal against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, it requires that you cover the tip of the bone, as long as the instruments have control over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, if you have an appropriate tool for this purpose, such as a scalpel or a fine awl, then with your strength; then reposition that which is staying in the hard part of the bone and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels intense pain afterwards, you should know it hasn't been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you place it so that it's in its natural position, then moisten the dressing with tannic black wine, and properly if this is in good condition; and don't put wax or anything else on the wound where there's ointment, as it might lead to infection and decay; then administer herbs when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover everything surrounding it according to the size of the wound, and make sure that the wound is not restricted by breaking; many times this has been done by fools, causing harm or decay in the patient one way or another; and the compresses should be softer and less destructive than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that an accident might have happened there, as we have said before, and you find pain in your hand, it doesn't suit to place splints; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and secure them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two days that the wound is swelling, remove what you have placed with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as the quadrifarmaceutical ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is united and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be so that the joints of the limb are put together in such a way that the bone slips down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if this continues day after day, and it cannot be joined but stays like that, know that there are small bone pieces causing pain due to which you should cover the wound with a tent, and remove all these pieces of dead tissue that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the wound, or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he explained in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when bone is broken and exposed in the body, as with the bone of the elbow or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not attempt to set it because many times this leads to death. Instead, leave it until it heals naturally; by chance, the pus will come out from him after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can. If you cannot, just leave it as it is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The burns come many times after the healing of the burn wound, even when it's close to the joint. A strange thing is to see the shape of the limb; and by chance it cannot perform its natural acts on the limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when this thing is fresh: if you administer stiffening medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, along with sarsaparilla, licorice, and other similar things, do so according to your preference or combine them all, mixing them with stictic wine or with plenty of egg or with garlic; then apply them on the wound in poultices, apply them well, and don't remove it by hand for days; then remove it, and start another poultice as long as the pustules are removed; or you can apply over a piece of plaster that has been made properly; because the properties of plaster allow to remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the pustule has hardened like stone and needs removal, cut through it from above, revealing excess fluid; or have it sanded by someone until it is removed, and continue treatment until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb which becomes weak after the siege (or after a period of confinement or hard work)
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and afterwards the limbs remain weak and delicate, this can happen for various reasons: due to which it was bound too tightly and wasn't bound as it should have been; or due to there being too many bindings, and not being able to bring the respiration to the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to too large movements, not in its time; or due to having little blood in his body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat well, and make the body soft until the healing spreads in him; then give them baths, and provide them joy and comfort. Then apply grease on the limb so that the grease attracts to the main respiration, and washes it with water often, until the respiration matches the limb. And restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken openly, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: nor should one believe those who say that we must break the entire limb anew. And many foolish people have done this in our land; these procedures are criticized, and they bring great harms, even causing death at times. However, if the dislocations and pains are still fresh, you should heat them with hot water or cook soothing herbs such as leaves of comfrey, roots, and mallow, among others; and apply a moistening plaster, like well-made yarrow. You take the comfrey sap and mix it with lard or oil from saffron, and make a plaster from that; or you take greased figs, grind them with bran, and other medicines that are made soothing by heating.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the node removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be gentle movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation has become old and hardened like bone, requiring treatment with an iron instrument, so it should be cut up to the bone at a subtle incision lightly; and place supervision and diligence in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the body.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects no particular area but now requires immediate restoration without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limbs swell, and by chance one might place points in their swollen state; this should not be done when moving them at the hour they are swollen: many times it leads to pus and other pains. Nevertheless, when such happens, make the patient rest until the abscesses subside; then immerse the limb in warm water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and cure each limb as it seems right for their state.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up until here.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated and downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat ossified at their joints and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the feet, causing saliva from the mouth to spill out, and preventing them from closing their mouths, as well as wrapping their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is complete and carried out, you should remove the cautery quickly, without hesitation; and in such a way that the surgeons prick the neck of the patient near the illness, and place the nails at the root of the dislocation of the jawbone within the mouth, if the dislocation involves two parts; and the other hand must be pulled out with both hands to ensure they are even; instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And keep pushing until she wakes up in her place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it causes pain, in the same way, if they are two jaws together, then use hot water and oil, as long as you gently reset them; don't overly force the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well sealed with soothing, then apply wet bandages in a poultice made from rosy oil and beeswax, then bind them lightly with moist string; let the patient rest on their back, and their limbs should be placed between two cushions, so they don't move neither to the right nor to the left, nor try to stretch too much, but should eat light food until the pains are eased, and the jaws are set firmly in place; then allow them to drink and dine lightly, without opening their mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set properly within an hour and are not returned to their original position, this results in fevers and recurrent illnesses, as well as occasional abdominal discomfort or vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is loss; and many times, death befalls the one who experiences it within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the forcefulness
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve the pain from within or below, it relieves only when outside, and one certainly feels this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then press with your palm to form a shape, and it will return; then place on the plaster and the bandage, and tighten; and if there's any pus in front of the wound, it cannot become dislocated; but if it does, reset it at its original location, as we said before; then place on the plaster and the bandage, and tighten, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus similarly is brought back the shoulder blades when they have been removed from their socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	On the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder dislocation occurs according to three ways: out of which one is that it dislocates at the part of the acromion below; and the second is at the part near the heel; and by chance dislocates at the part above, this happens very rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and it gets dislocated repeatedly from under towards the acromion, even in those with little flesh, because they tend to do so quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out and then comes back in.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens in some men due to impact or bruising, and the shoulder swells up with an abscess and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you must verify it as long as you are sure about it; and only after that start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And understand the dislocations when it goes down towards the acromion, and makes a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their obvious diversity; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and from the acromion to the deltoid region of the shoulder, just like if it were an eye. And the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move with any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not completely hidden, because you find it clearly at the clavicle; and this way of dislocation can only be restored when it is new, or when there is a baby in the mother.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts his hand from the ailment up top, then places his fingers on the surface, and lifts the joint up forcefully to its original position; and the minister lifts his hand, extends it upwards, placing it onto [the affected area]; if it moves too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come as we have said within a few days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and apply soothing, calming remedies, such as decoctions of rue, fenugreek, and tansy in warm water, then apply this. Then bandage the patient's backside, place wool under their armpit, not too soft nor too hard. Next place your fingers on their heel under the wool, lift up their shoulder with a strong but gentle movement, guide your hand down towards the ailment; and another assistant should cut off the top of their shoulder so that it doesn't move downwards. That shoulder is now back in position, if you see that it has been correctly reset this way: And it's necessary for there to be someone larger than the patient present at home during this process; and stand straight towards the side, prop up your shoulder under the patient’s assistant, lift up the armpit high so that the patient hangs down in a curve; then another assistant should guide their hand downwards of the patient towards their abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if they let the patient become too light, to carry him with no weight at all, then the dislocation comes back immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reset may also be done in another way: and you stick the long stake into the ground, so that the limb is also bent like a bow, and it's neither too big nor too soft; then place it under the patient, but let there be soil beneath it, and the limb must stay long enough with the shaft; then stretch out his hand from below on the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place very quickly; and if it doesn't return through all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take a stake of two arms wide and three fingers thick, which has a head round enough to enter almost completely under the arch, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then bind the head to the stick under a shield so that the stick doesn't hurt the hair, then place the stick on the shoulder at an angle with the hair; and extend your arm up along the stick as long as possible, then tie the support on the stick, and the arm below the head, then put the arm on one of two thick rods, about four inches wide, and have your hand extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return to its place right now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, in whatever manner, if you need to place an equal thread on the shoulder joint, then apply plaster powder mixed with mill dust, along with incense and yolk butter, all over the shoulder and around it, then remove from the shoulder area, and retie above the plaster dressing, and secure the bandage again on top of the plaster, and hold hands to their necks, and keep the hands in this manner.

And when dislocations are in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg promptly, and according to what I have said; and place the pain of being on the bad side, then press with the other hand, and pull forward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, it does not suit to extend the patient's head down nor lift them up from the earth. Instead, they should remain like how their hip was when it was dislocated in front, just as we said about lying on both hips; and they should be lying flat with their knees extended just as we said before, and pressure must be applied at the joint table; then it's correct when the patient can extend their legs, and they will be level. Then adjust the thighs, put the plaster on, and hold it tightly with one band, so that the hip does not move. Rest for three days or four, then release them, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, apply pressure as before, and leave them for three more days; then release them and allow them to walk comfortably until their limbs have been strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees can be dislocated in two ways: this means, internally and externally, and behind; and they do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs for this are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if they cannot reach their knee, you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is done by making the patient stand upright, stretching out their leg if possible, placing their back against your waist, placing their foot on yours; then take their kneecap between your palms, pull apart with your fingers, then bend both sides slightly at the knee joints; and have another attendant stretch out their foot as long as the knees return to their place, and the signs are that they comfortably bend their leg at the knee lightly; and place the plaster on, make the leg and thigh touch firmly for three or four days, then release; and do not disturb the patient's movement until the limbs have become strong.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not broken, then apply strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never properly set and never fully released, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle swells and tends forward to the part where it is dislocated; the return is swift, and one should gently extend its hands when it is merely being held.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, then have the patient lie straight, and hold them upright with their legs apart at the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left, twice, before lifting it upwards and firmly pushing down on it; do this again, as we have said, while pulling and moving the foot down. If it returns, that is well; if not, restart the process, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this manner, then have the patient stand behind their back with the floor, plant one leg firmly between their buttocks, and tie a cloth tightly around them to prevent any friction on the leg. Then trim the legs of the patient, and with others lift the foot when extended towards you or to your side, where they tie it up to the collarbone; then evenly extend each assistant's hands, and place the sandbag so that it is firmly between the buttocks for holding the leg as it is lifted; finally, hold the dislocation evenly in both hands, and with others trim the healthy leg at about the ankle, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the point, then place the plaster and bind above, apply strength to shape, tie the limb to the leg, guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, making sure not to tie too tightly; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, remove the tension. Then, on the third day or fourth, let go of most of the movement, allow the patient to walk for another three days; and if it progresses past this stage, it is still not certain that it will no longer dislocate.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus comes out, you should soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	From these two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both shoulders are dislocated, if they suit well to extend them by work, and this is a slight matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in neither the back nor at the feet, you should have the patient lie on their full length or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot until it returns; and when they are equal and there's nothing opening, place under the sole of the foot a table for two shoulders, then apply pressure and let them stay for three days, then release them; and make them rest until they recover.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Regarding wounds and dislocations combined
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, many times the patient dies: if not to be overconfident in treatment, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for long periods, and if you are not kind and merciful and considerate, do not be rash; at first use things that soothe the wound until it is bandaged, and leave the patient with God, if you do not see hope of recovery; and when you see hope, immediately set the member in place as you can, so that wounds are drained and heal; and when the member is in place, use things that soothe the wound until they heal, treat the wound properly using desiccated ointments; and if with dislocation there is fracture and small bones have broken out, fix them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and guard against entering a path of fear according to what I said, for this will bring you to your Creator's will, and through knowledge arm yourself and care for your body.
Amen	Amen
